Soviet Union Celebrates Aviation Day; Amazing Flight Techniques Performed Over Moscow; Air Force Commander Declares Efforts to Fulfill Four Conditions 19

(Moscow) The nation celebrated Aviation Day today. Air Force officers performed various flight demonstrations at the Tushino Airfield. Guests included members of the diplomatic corps, journalists, representatives from various countries attending the International Congress of Physiologists and the Third International Congress. Air Force Commander Alksnis gave a speech, stating that "the Soviet aviation sector should fulfill four conditions: (1) Enhance the combat capabilities of Soviet aircraft; (2) Ensure aviation safety; (3) Increase the production volume of the aircraft industry; and (4) Prepare for the rapid production of large quantities of certain aircraft during peacetime." (18th Havas News Agency)

(Moscow) The Soviet Aviation Day was celebrated at this airfield today. Party and government leaders, diplomatic corps representatives, and over one hundred thousand spectators attended the event to watch demonstrations of high-speed aircraft and fighter jets. During their performance, advanced flight techniques such as tumbling and various formations were used. Afterwards, there was a flight parade composed of passenger planes and gliders, as well as a demonstration of light aircraft. Their exhaustiveness and perfect technology, also performing tumbling flights and arranging formations. The focus of this demonstration was on safe parachute jumping. At that time, six airplanes carried 150 jumpers to jump down, either using delayed parachute opening or collective jumping methods. At the end of the celebration, three light aircraft soared across the entire venue. Today, large-scale celebrations were held in various parks in Moscow, with hundreds of thousands of participants. (18th TASS News Agency)

(Moscow) August 18th is the Soviet Aviation Day. During the celebration held today, the great achievements of Soviet civil aviation, flight technology, and aviation entertainment were fully demonstrated.

Dugachev, the Director of the Soviet Civil Aviation Administration, published an article in Pravda, stating that the Soviet Union's air routes this year total more than 70,000 kilometers, with 111,000 passengers to be carried, 11,500 tons of mail and cargo, 120,000 hectares of aircraft seeding, 600,000 hectares of aircraft pest control, and 3 million hectares of aircraft spraying for malaria prevention. Izvestia reported, "The Soviet Union now has 113 aviation clubs, with thousands of young amateurs learning aviation here. The Soviet Union also has more than 500,000 aircraft model designers. In 1934, there were 1,400 glider training classes, training 18,000 people to drive gliders. Parachute jumping has been held hundreds of thousands of times, and there are hundreds of parachute jumping platforms across the country." The newspaper's editorial stated, "Our country's inexhaustible creative power has enabled us to create the world's most heroic, grand, and invincible air force in a short period of time. Aviation was originally a tool of destruction and death, but we have transformed it into a driving force for promoting culture and affluent living. The wings of our aviation team will carry peace to the whole world." (18th TASS News Agency)

False Release of Arrested Russians 20

(Harbin) Seven Russians arrested here last Thursday, who were identified by the "Manchu" authorities as having intentions to oppose "Manchu" behavior and obstruct the organization of the Russian Overseas Chinese Federation, have been released today. However, they must leave the "Manchu" territory before September 15. (19th Reuters)

Peace in East Africa Hanging by a Thread; Paris Conference Breaks Down; Italy Determined to Make Abyssinia a Protectorate; British and French Mediation Efforts Fail 21

(Paris) The tripartite conference on the Italian-Abyssinian dispute failed last night, and a war in Africa may not be avoided. Britain and France had previously proposed to Italy a suggestion regarding the concession of economic rights to Abyssinia, which reportedly included three conditions: (1) Maintaining Abyssinia's political independence and territorial integrity; (2) Abyssinia's agreement; (3) The League of Nations' agreement. Last night, Italian Representative Aloisi brought Italian Prime Minister Mussolini's reply to the meeting. The British and French representatives both considered it unsatisfactory and announced an adjournment of the meeting.

Joint Communiqué Issued

A communiqué signed by Laval, Eden, and Aloisi was subsequently issued, stating that the three statesmen gathered to seek a peaceful resolution to the Italian-Abyssinian dispute, but ultimately failed to find a basis for discussion that could resolve the dispute. The difficulties encountered in formulating suggestions require an announcement of adjournment, and future discussions will continue through diplomatic channels. (19th Reuters)

Main Reason for the Breakdown of Negotiations

British Minister for League of Nations Affairs Eden and Italian Representative Aloisi will meet with Laval once more tomorrow before departing for their respective countries. It is reported that the main reason for the stalemate in the talks is that Italy is determined to take at least a portion of Abyssinia as an Italian protectorate. This objective of Italy has met with two obstacles: Firstly, the Abyssinian Emperor is determined to oppose territorial concessions; Secondly, British Minister for League of Nations Affairs Eden is also determined to abide by the obligations in the League of Nations Covenant to guarantee the territorial integrity and political independence of member states. Therefore, the negotiations have broken down. The suggestions jointly proposed by Britain and France are divided into three items: (1) Giving Italy broad possibilities to develop the economy in Abyssinia; (2) Ensuring the security of the borders of Italian territories in East Africa; (3) Protecting Italian immigrants within Abyssinia. This suggestion does not conflict with the League of Nations Covenant, and Abyssinia would also be happy to accept it because its territorial integrity and political independence can be maintained. Unfortunately, Italy resolutely refused, and the negotiations had to be halted. (18th Havas News Agency)

League of Nations Achievement Unlikely

(Geneva) The breakdown of the Paris tripartite conference is astonishing. The only remaining hope for averting the war in Africa lies in the League of Nations Council meeting to be held on September 4. People in the League of Nations all feel that practical results cannot be achieved by mere talks, but no one knows what will be done other than empty talk.

Laval said that he has not given up hope for averting the war, as the League of Nations Council meeting on September 4 could make a final effort. However, Eden does not have such wishful thinking. Italy's demands are effectively seeking to make Abyssinia its protectorate. Unless Italy reduces this demand, it will be difficult to reach a negotiated resolution before the League of Nations Council meeting. Judging from the attitude of the Italian delegation, Italy does not seem likely to make any concessions. (19th Reuters)

Italian Prime Minister Says No Hope is Dashed

(Paris) Italian Prime Minister Mussolini's one word "no" in a telegram today has completely dashed the hope of the tripartite conference preventing the East African war. After Italy rejected the British and French proposals, the tripartite conference issued a communiqué this morning, stating that because "difficulties have arisen after considering all proposals," it announced an adjournment of the meeting. However, future research will be conducted through diplomatic channels. (18th Guomin News Agency) The Italian government's attitude towards the British and French proposals has not greatly surprised the parties involved in the conference, as the Italian delegation had a tough attitude from the beginning, so it was known early on that there would be no good results. The main difficulty now is Italy's demand for political suzerainty over Abyssinia. It is heard that the British delegation firmly opposes this concession of rights, and the French representative is trying to find a solution that satisfies both parties, so it is suggested that the Abyssinian government hire Italian consultants, so that Italy can gain special political influence in Abyssinia without conflicting with Abyssinia's sovereignty and the provisions of the League of Nations Covenant. However, Italian Prime Minister Mussolini is still not satisfied and insists on obtaining broader political rights in Abyssinia. (19th Reuters)

British and Italian Representatives Leave Paris

(Paris) Italian Representative Aloisi will visit French Prime Minister Laval before starting his journey back to Rome tonight. (19th Reuters)

(Paris) French Prime Minister Laval met with British Representative Eden this morning and then received Italian Representative Aloisi. Laval and Eden both believe that the British and French governments must now focus their efforts on preparing for the League of Nations Council meeting in Geneva on September 4. Britain and France will liaise closely with each other diplomatically on this matter. Eden met with the Abyssinian ambassador to France at the British Embassy at 11:00 AM this morning and explained the progress of the tripartite conference. It is heard that the British delegation will return to London by train this afternoon, while Eden may delay slightly. (19th Reuters)

To Cope with the Future Situation, Britain Must Consider Three Things; Cabinet to Hold Emergency Meeting; Lifting the Arms Embargo Under Discussion 22

(London) After the failure of the Paris tripartite conference, the British Cabinet is discussing the matter. Eden will arrive in London tonight. Foreign Secretary Runciman and Baldwin MacDonald had a phone conversation. They will now return to London from Norfolk and will likely reconsider the issue of the arms embargo on Abyssinia. Currently, Britain generally does not issue export licenses for arms destined for Italy or Abyssinia. (19th Reuters)

(London) Foreign Secretary Hoare, who was vacationing in Norfolk, will rush back to London tonight to immediately consider the consequences of the failure of the Paris tripartite conference. There are three issues that the British Cabinet should consider: (1) The issue of the arms embargo on Italy and Abyssinia; (2) Protecting the American Embassy in the Abyssinian capital; (3) Increasing the number of troops in the British territories bordering Abyssinia. Italian Representative Aloisi made a statement at the Paris conference regarding Britain's rights to the Blue Nile water source. This statement changed the original state of British-Italian relations. The British side is deeply concerned that Italy will no longer respect the 1925 treaty, which threatens the cotton planting plan in Egypt, as planting cotton is the basic plan related to the Egyptian economy, and planting cotton on a large scale in Egypt requires adjusting the Nile water conservancy first. However, before fully understanding France's attitude, the British government will not fully determine its attitude in Geneva. Liberal and Labour public opinion both demand that Britain take strong anti-Italian action in Geneva. The Liberal Party's newspaper, the "Manchester Guardian," even suggested imposing a mineral embargo on Italy, believing that if Italy cannot import certain essential minerals, it will not be able to wage war on Abyssinia. However, it is generally believed that although the British government cannot ignore general public opinion, especially before the general election, the government cannot but have some concerns, but the government's attitude will not be as resolute as that of the Liberal Party and the Labour Party. (19th Havas News Agency)

France in a Dilemma; Believes the Door to Negotiations is Not Closed; Will Continue to Act as a Mediator 23

(Paris) Today, Eden visited Laval to discuss the aftermath, but they have not yet had a thorough discussion on the policies they intend to take at the League of Nations meeting. No one in British and French circles dares to expect the League of Nations meeting to be successful. However, Laval will be heartbroken if this meeting fails again, because Laval has displayed his extraordinary talent as a mediator, but has ultimately failed to gain Italy's understanding. France's position is now particularly complex. On the one hand, it is cooperating with Britain to support the League of Nations and is eager to eliminate the war. On the other hand, it is extremely unwilling to offend Italy and endanger its newly established French-Italian friendship, which is so beneficial to it in Europe. (19th Reuters)

(Paris) According to responsible sources, although the British, French, and Italian tripartite conference has announced an adjournment, the door to negotiations in Paris cannot be considered completely closed. As for the French government's position, it remains committed to respecting the principles of the League of Nations Covenant and has not changed. France's policy towards Geneva is in line with the position taken by Britain. In addition, France has a deep friendship with Italy. The French delegation has made every effort to mediate in this tripartite conference, and will continue to do its best to mediate in the future, and will not interrupt it due to the adjournment of the tripartite conference. (18th Havas News Agency)

British Newspapers Criticize Italy for Disregarding the League of Nations

(London) The Times newspaper said in an editorial today that the seriousness of Italy's decision on the proposals put forward by the Paris tripartite conference is unthinkable. The League of Nations is a tool for Italy to obtain justice, but Italy is going back on its word and disregarding the League of Nations. If Mussolini's current attitude remains unchanged, then a direct conflict between Italy and the League of Nations will be unavoidable when the League of Nations Council meets in the future. It is now necessary to seek a solution that does not conflict with the principles of the League of Nations, otherwise the League of Nations Covenant will become a dead letter. If the League of Nations does not exist, or the League of Nations is reduced to a ridiculous and incompetent position, then European peace will only depend on new and less hopeful institutions to prevent reckless behavior. For Britain, this issue is extremely important. For France, it is even more important. (19th Reuters)

French Newspapers Worry About the Future of Europe

(Paris) "Le Petit Parisien," "L'Action Française," and "L'Écho de Paris" all expressed pessimism about the adjournment of the British, French, and Italian tripartite conference, fearing that the Italian-Abyssinian war is unavoidable. Among them, "Le Petit Parisien" said that if British public opinion urges its government to take a tough stance based on the League of Nations Covenant, Italy may withdraw from the League of Nations. However, if the East African conflict continues, the League of Nations Council may convene to seize the opportunity to seek a peaceful solution. "L'Écho de Paris" said, "Does Italian Prime Minister Mussolini intend to avenge the humiliation of the Battle of Adwa? (In the Battle of Adwa in 1896, the Italian army was defeated by Abyssinia) Does he intend to revitalize Italy's military might and make Abyssinia its colony? If Mussolini really has this ambition, then no matter how much effort is spent, it may not be possible to stop it. If so, when the League of Nations Council meets on September 4, British Minister for League of Nations Affairs Eden will inevitably unfold the file on Italy's responsibilities, and Laval will only have to abide by the Council's decision, and Italy will declare its withdrawal from the League of Nations. The League of Nations is afraid that it will not be able to support itself after this crisis, and the collective security system will collapse with it. At that time, France will personally see Germany rise and put pressure on Austria. The seriousness of the European situation is self-evident. For this reason, France's situation is very difficult. In order to avoid this danger, France must cooperate with Britain on the one hand, and must also liaise with Rome on the other. If not, Italy will break the peace discipline without any scruples and will turn to Germany to conspire to cause trouble. This is something that must be prevented in advance." (19th Havas News Agency)

The Turn of September and October: Warfare Expected Imminently, Italy Determined to Eradicate Ethiopia; Soldiers and Munitions Ceaselessly Transported to Eastern Africa 24

(Rome) Roman figures are not surprised nor regretful about the outcome of the Paris Tripartite Conference. It is said that the final thing Italy desired was reconciliation. The Italian government is now determined to conquer Abyssinia, and then economically and politically control the country through military occupation. Italian circles believe that the League of Nations Administrative Council meeting scheduled for September 4th is unlikely to be more successful than the Paris Conference, and may even have more serious consequences. Italy now feels that America's attempt to eliminate the war has made it more likely for Italy to withdraw from the League of Nations than a month ago. People in Rome all say that no matter what the League of Nations and Britain do, the Italian army will invade Abyssinia in October. This can be predicted in advance. (Reuters, 19th)

Naples, Italy: The mail ship "Vinci" carrying 50 officers, 1,000 artillerymen, and a large amount of munitions, set sail for the port of Massawa in East Africa. Another ship, "Gianfranco," also departed at the same time carrying military supplies. Government representatives and crowds cheered and wished them well as the ship was unmoored. (Havas, 18th)

Cairo: This week, the number of Italian ships transporting troops and military supplies through the Suez Canal has increased unprecedentedly. Today, a total of twelve Italian ships, large and small, passed through the canal, all packed full of military supplies. Even the decks had almost no empty space. There were countless tanks, artillery vehicles, armored vehicles, and automated cargo trucks, as well as a mobile crane and countless mules and horses. However, the ships returning from East Africa were mostly empty, or only carried sick soldiers. According to estimates from banking and aviation circles, the Italian government has paid 750,000 pounds in Suez Canal passage fees. (Guomin News Agency, 19th)

Abyssinia Lacks New Medical Knowledge

(Paris) Since the outbreak of the Italo-Abyssinian dispute, although the general public wants to know the general situation of medicine in Abyssinia, they suffer from the lack of people who are familiar with the details. Dr. Martini, the French director of the hospital established by former Abyssinian Emperor Menelik II in Addis Ababa, has made some publications on this issue for reference. The main points are as follows: "Strictly speaking, there is no medicine in Abyssinia. The general public has little faith in the local indigenous doctors, and rarely consults foreign doctors, whether they are Europeans, Syrians, or Indians. These foreign doctors often do not have formal medical certificates, so it is natural that they cannot gain the faith of the Abyssinian people. Therefore, those who are ill mostly seek treatment from witch doctors. Only when they have no other choice do they seek diagnosis and treatment from these mediocre doctors who have learned from experience but lack basic knowledge. If one place is ineffective, they change to another place, and some even change to four or five places or more. These mediocre doctors charge extremely high prices, causing people to have a bad impression, thinking that medical treatment is simple in procedure but extremely expensive in cost. Therefore, they all hesitate and are unwilling to try it lightly unless absolutely necessary. The Abyssinian Emperor, in view of this, established several hospitals, and the hospital presided over by Dr. Martini is the most famous. Dr. Martini has studied the special circumstances of Abyssinian people's illnesses for many years and has gained a lot of experience. He has published papers in the "Medical Century" magazine, and some of his theories coincide with those recently discovered by other scholars in Europe. Therefore, Dr. Martini can be called the most contributing person to Abyssinian medicine. However, although the establishment of hospitals is roughly scaled, surgical equipment is still lacking in places other than a corner of the Abyssinian capital. In the event of war with foreign countries, it is necessary to recruit surgical doctors, assistants, and all necessary equipment from Europe. This issue is now being considered by the Abyssinian authorities. As for the most prevalent disease in Abyssinia, venereal disease affects 50% of the national population, but its cause is mostly hereditary, so after several generations, the effect of the bacteria has been reduced. Abyssinian people mostly use a very clumsy method to treat this disease. A goat is placed in the same room as the patient, and the doors and windows are tightly closed. A brazier is lit in the room to gradually increase the heat, because the only principle of treating venereal disease in Abyssinia is to "feed the bacteria" as much as possible, and strong heat and avoiding wind and light are good methods for treating all diseases. If the bacteria are not properly fed, the patient will be swallowed by the "bacteria." Therefore, the patient must skin the goat in the hot room, drink its blood, and eat twelve parts of the goat's body raw, accompanied by fine wine, until drunk and full. The amount of food is so abundant that if a European were to take it, they would be so full that they would die. This is because it does not conform to the above-mentioned principle of properly feeding the bacteria. After eating like this for four or five months, sores will inevitably appear all over the patient's body. At this time, they must go to hot springs to bathe. The most famous is "Philhoa Spring." In addition to bathing in it, patients must also scoop up and drink its water. Although there are many skin disease patients filling the spring, everyone drinks the water as usual without any scruples. After bathing in the hot springs for a considerable period of time, the patient must be placed in a tent with a brazier lit inside to make the patient sweat a lot, and inject a medicinal juice. After forty days, the disease will be cured and will never recur. This treatment method has been passed down through generations by the Abyssinian people, and they all believe in it without a doubt. It still has the faith of the general public today. It goes without saying that it does not conform to the principles of new medicine. In addition, Abyssinia has a special "panacea" that is famous all over the world, commonly known as "Cusso," which is made by soaking several kinds of red and white flowers. Its efficacy is so broad that it can treat almost all diseases, such as enhancing digestion, clearing blood, detoxifying, and treating poison injuries. The Abyssinian people like to eat raw meat the most, so they take this medicine the most. In short, Abyssinian medicine is clumsy and crude in terms of the old, and simple and crude in terms of the new. The most dominant force is still the old customs of the witch doctors. Although the Abyssinian Emperor is making every effort to introduce new medical knowledge, the traditional forces are still hindering it, and the foreign doctors who come here are also superficial and insufficient to meet people's expectations. Therefore, the progress of promoting new medicine is extremely slow." (Havas, 18th)

The current rise in Anglo-American exchange rates is evidence of this. Furthermore, Britain has sent personnel to investigate China's currency problem. Japanese Foreign Minister Hirota Refreshes Diplomatic Ranks; Major Reshuffle of Overseas Personnel Imminent 31

(Tokyo) Foreign Minister Hirota said that at the end of last month, the directors and ministers of the ministry had suggested to the minister and vice minister that it was necessary to carry out the reorganization of senior officials and imperial officials in order to improve diplomatic efficiency. Moreover, administrative officials also submitted a written opinion on diplomatic reform. Therefore, it was decided to take the opportunity of the regular changes in December to make major reforms. The purpose of the changes is to improve diplomatic efficiency, and the aim is to inject fresh air. This move is enough to be a touchstone for the abilities of Foreign Minister Hirota and Vice Minister Shigemitsu. The fundamental principles of this reform are roughly as follows: (1) Ambassadors and ministers-level officials who are currently on standby will be allowed to retire from active duty when their standby period expires, or they will voluntarily request retirement. However, even those who are on standby and capable can still be reused. (2) Among the active ambassadors and ministers, those who have stayed for more than two terms will, in principle, be required to resign voluntarily. (3) Higher officials below the rank of imperial appointees who have been in their current positions for a long time and cannot be promoted to senior officials or mandated appointees will be allowed to retire before December. (4) There is a need to reorganize the personnel efficiency of the consuls-general, section chiefs, and consuls of the third, fourth, and fifth classes of higher officials, many of whom are special appointees from the war. About ten to fifteen people will be reorganized. (5) In principle, the reorganization of those below the rank of imperial appointees will recall those currently working overseas. Section chiefs and administrative officials working in the ministry will be excluded from the scope of the reorganization. (Den-tsu News Agency, 19th)

Impressions of a Southern Tour 59

— Special Correspondent Qian Hua

(XIV) The Tight Organization of the Reception

The first group of more than 180 annual meeting members, divided among the Guiqiang, Guide, and Xinyiean steamships, departed Wuzhou at 11 PM on the 8th, heading directly to Nanning. Ma Junwu, the president of Guangxi University, and others personally boarded the ships to bid farewell. Each ship carried only over 200 tons and had 90 horsepower, yet it carried 50 to 60 passengers, feeling particularly crowded. The Wuzhou reception office initially planned to have a portion travel by car, but ultimately abandoned the idea due to the rising water level and muddy roads. Instead, female guests stayed in the cabins, and most male guests slept on the floor. Dozens of people lived in one room, the air was murky, and at first, it was quite painful. Overnight, everyone felt calm and collected, and the river breeze was gentle, eliminating the heat, turning it into enjoyment. Along the river, the water level rose, and the current was rapid. Initially, there were many plains on both sides, with distant mountains faintly visible. After reaching Guiping, the mountains became precipitous, mostly protruding from the plains, forming vertical shapes, or connecting like pen rests, or like a giant stone bamboo shoot. In Chinese paintings, we often see mountain paintings depicting such bizarre mountain shapes, thinking that they were the fantasies of artists, deliberately made bizarre, but now we have finally seen them in person. Those on the boat who had not traveled to Guangxi all pointed and gazed from the windows. According to those who had traveled there, after passing this point, these strange mountains are everywhere, especially in Guilin, common sights, and not surprising. The ship briefly docked at Pingnan, Guiping, Guixian, Hengxian, and Yongchun. Boatmen relied on the ship to sell fruits, food, and other things, vying to buy them, business was booming. Things like pineapples, bananas, star fruit, longan, etc. were all extremely fresh, sweet, and delicious. There is also a famous fruit called Huangpi, Guangxi's is the best, its shape is similar to longan, but it has many pits and is sweet, and the skin is particularly fragrant. The ship arrived in Nanning on the morning of the 11th. Guangxi authorities sent personnel to board the ship to welcome them and prepared a large number of carts. Banners welcoming the annual meeting were hung along the way, with words asking for guidance and criticism of Guangxi's construction. The streets were tidy, and the atmosphere was solemn. Westerners and Japanese people stayed at the Qunle Society, a magnificent and elegant building, similar to a club, almost like a YMCA. It had facilities such as a swimming pool and tennis court, and offered complete Western-style services. The rest were housed in various reception centers, also very comfortable and considerate. The Guangxi authorities formed a reception committee, providing diligent hospitality, with no detail spared. The organization of each group was extremely tight, with no confusion at all. Everything was in good order, proving the effectiveness of daily training, which cannot be achieved overnight. As the saying goes, "Observe a person in small details." From this, we can get a glimpse of Guangxi's achievements.

(XV) The Academic Qualifications of Foreign Members

This joint annual meeting of six academic groups held in Nanning, gathering academic circles from all over the country in one place, is truly an unprecedented event. The members who came to participate were divided into groups: Hebei, Tianjin, Shandong, Henan, Shaanxi, and Shanxi were one group, Hunan, Hubei, Jiangxi, and Anhui were one group, Jiangsu and Zhejiang were one group, Fujian and Guangdong were one group, and Sichuan and Yunnan were another group. Each province had scholars, and Guangdong accounted for the largest number due to its proximity. Therefore, the languages in the annual meeting were mainly Cantonese, Mandarin, and Shanghainese. Among the foreign members, there was (1) Professor Hacks of the Geography Department of National Central University from Austria, who also presented a paper titled "Classification of Austrian Topography." (2) Dr. Zha Shi, a German linguist, who could speak seven languages including Chinese, English, Russian, French, German, Japanese, and Latin, and spoke Mandarin particularly fluently. (3) Mr. and Mrs. Wallace, zoology professors from Lingnan University. (4) Mr. and Mrs. Hofman, chemistry professors from Lumei University. (5) Ms. Li Fushi, a biology professor from Jinling Women's University. And three Japanese researchers from the Shanghai Institute of Natural Sciences: Ren Shui Songichiro, Kimura Koichi, and Higashinaka Hideo, who were researching Chinese medicine and geography, all had papers. Kimura's paper was titled "Research on Chinese Dendrobium," which was of some value. Among all the Chinese members, university professors were the majority, followed by middle school teachers. Famous domestic universities such as National Central University, Yenching University, Tsinghua University, Nankai University, Jinling Women's University, Sun Yat-sen University, and Lingnan University all participated. However, apart from the foreign members, many of the papers presented by Chinese members were also written in English, which was the biggest shortcoming. If it is for the convenience of foreigners to read, then there is no need to hold a meeting in China. If they feel that it is difficult to find accurate translations for specialized terms, they might as well include the terms in both Chinese and English. If it is for showing off and wanting to demonstrate their expertise in foreign literature, then it reflects their ignorance of Chinese studies, which is also not a good idea.

International Commercial Telegram August 19th Reuters Special Business Report 60

Gold and Silver

British Gold: The London gold price today was 140 shillings and 2.5 pence, down 1.5 pence.

British Silver: The London silver market experienced a slight loosening in price due to some selling from the East. Spot prices fell 0.0625 to 29 pence, futures fell 0.125 to 28.9375 pence. India and China sold, the United States bought. The market closed steadily.

Exchange Rates

British-American: The London foreign exchange market opened steadily this morning, but the US dollar fell sharply within the first hour. The British-American exchange rate opened at 4 yuan, 9 jiao, 7 fen, 0625, lower than the closing price on Saturday and Sunday by 0.0625. Within the first hour, it rose by 75 to 4 yuan, 9 jiao, 7 fen, 8125, then fell by 125 at noon to 4 yuan, 9 jiao, 7 fen, 6875, after which there were no changes.

British-French: The opening price rose by 4 pounds to 74 francs 94. It rose by 7 pounds in the first hour to 75 francs 01. The price remained unchanged until 2 PM.

Cotton and Wheat

American Cotton: The New York cotton market opened quietly, with merchants adopting a wait-and-see attitude. Although the Liverpool cotton market was relatively stable, prices here fell sharply at the opening due to the lack of indication of government loan policies, but gradually recovered later.

British Wheat: The Liverpool wheat market was quiet this morning due to the political instability, but prices were stable. At 1 PM, the October futures price was 5 shillings and 3.75 pence, up 0.25 from the closing price on Saturday and Sunday.

American Wheat: The Chicago wheat market opened slightly higher due to the rise in prices in Liverpool, but soon fell below the closing price on Saturday. There was a lack of interest. Grains, due to the continued favorable climate and agricultural reports, were mostly liquidated, leading to lower prices after the opening.

British Cotton: The Liverpool cotton market was slightly looser. At 1 PM, the October futures price was 5.99, down 2 points.

Rubber

London: The London rubber market was quiet at the opening, with prices falling slightly, but soon stabilized. At noon, the trading price for October-December futures was 5.8125 pence, the same as the closing price on Friday.

New York: The New York rubber market opened slightly lower, then turned stable. Outside interest in rubber remains lacking.

Securities

New York: The situation in the New York stock market was inconsistent after opening this morning. Public utility stocks fell sharply at the opening due to various reform plans to be discussed and passed by Congress before its adjournment. Power plant stocks fell slightly at the opening and then recovered, but other electrical stocks were weak. Railroad stocks were also looser. Other stocks opened steadily and then showed some mixed performance. Steel stocks remained firm due to improved business. Oil stocks had slight demand. New York Commodity Market Prices

Hubei Province Distributes Agricultural Relief Funds: 31 Counties Receive a Total of 430,000 Yuan in Relief; Disaster Relief Association Stipulates Measures for Distributing Seeds 61

Hankou Correspondence: Regarding agricultural relief in Hubei Province, the Flood Relief Association has raised 400,000 yuan and has begun distribution. The original selection of 28 counties with the most severe disasters has now been increased by 3 counties, totaling 31 counties. The relief committees for each county were appointed on the 16th and departed in different directions on the 17th. The relief funds are being distributed simultaneously today, totaling 9,568 yuan for Pi county, 15,369 yuan for Xiaogan, 10,125 yuan for Yingcheng, 17,310 yuan for Gucheng, 21,995 yuan for Mianyang, 14,399 yuan for Zhijiang, 10,992 yuan for Songzi, 14,349 yuan for Yun County, 5,736 yuan for Jun County, 11,784 yuan for Jingshan, 3,751 yuan for Xishui, 2,755 yuan for Dangyang, 4,017 yuan for Qichun, 40,965 yuan for Tianmen, 15,072 yuan for Hanyang, 22,774 yuan for Hanchuan, 16,509 yuan for Shishou, 20,580 yuan for Zhongxiang, 22,010 yuan for Xiangyang, 15,407 yuan for Yicheng, 35,489 yuan for Jiangling, 7,097 yuan for Yunmeng, 14,377 yuan for Qianjiang, 19,547 yuan for Gong'an, 15,410 yuan for Jianli, 8,035 yuan for Guanghua, 11,439 yuan for Yidu, 7,183 yuan for Jingmen, 991 yuan for Yuan'an, 2,248 yuan for Yunxi, 1,130 yuan for Jiayu, totaling 439,416 yuan in relief funds. The distribution is to be completed before the White Dew Festival on the 8th of next month. The Flood Relief Association has now stipulated the following measures: (1) The Association will provide seed subsidies to the counties most severely affected by the disaster and where autumn grain can be replanted. (2) The subsidy seed funds will be received by the county magistrate and purchased under the supervision of personnel sent by the Association. They will be distributed according to the number of disaster-stricken fields and extremely poor people in the county, not divided equally by funds. (3) Counties that cannot purchase seeds directly nearby will have them purchased by the Association and handed over to the county for receipt, still under the supervision of personnel sent by the Association. (4) The seeds needed for replanting autumn grain in each county will be purchased by the Association's committee together with the county magistrate, according to the local situation and season. (5) After the Association's committee members arrive in the county, they should cooperate with the county government to investigate each household in the area where seeds should be distributed, and create a clear list of the names and quantities of seeds to be received by those persons. To facilitate disaster victims’ receipt, they should imprint their right thumb fingerprint under their name to verify their identity. (6) After the distribution lists are completed, the distribution date and location should be posted in public places to allow disaster victims to go to receive them at the appointed time and place. (7) The distribution of seeds will use the city dou as the standard measure. (8) The seeds to be received by fleeing disaster victims shall not be received by others on their behalf. (9) Seeds that have not been received by fleeing disaster victims and remaining seeds shall be reported to the Association for instructions on how to handle them and shall not be misappropriated without authorization. (10) When the distribution of seeds requires the assistance of local teams and district Baoxia leaders, the county government will supervise them. (11) After the seeds are distributed, the committee of the wood should be distributed by the county government, listing the names and quantities of seed recipients by district, Bao, and Jia, and publicly announced at the original relief distribution locations. The relief distribution lists should be reported to the association for verification. (12) The transportation costs required for each county to purchase seeds may be covered by 5% of the seed fund received and accurately reported. (13) The committee members sent by this county shall not receive local supplies. (14) If the county magistrate of each county and the personnel assisting in relief work are found to have engaged in embezzlement and bribery, or are found to be untrue or incomplete, they will be severely punished in accordance with the regulations on punishment of relief personnel once the facts are verified. (17th)

Overview of Guangdong Province's Overseas Workers in the Last Six Months: Departures to the Americas Are Almost Zero; Departures to Nanyang Are Slightly More Than Before; Singapore Recently Imposed Entry Restrictions Again 62

Guangzhou Correspondence: Guangdong Province has always had a large number of overseas Chinese workers. Since the global recession spread, the number of unemployed overseas Chinese is overwhelming, and they have been forced to return to China. Those going to the Americas have traditionally been from Taishan, Kaiping, Enping, and Xinhui counties, while those going to Nanyang have traditionally been from Chaozhou, Meizhou, and Qiongya counties. Recently, due to the sharp drop in gold prices in the Americas, the economy of overseas Chinese in America has been greatly affected, and the US government has restricted the export of cash. The amount of money remitted back to their hometowns each year by overseas Chinese in America is less than one-tenth or two-tenths of what it used to be. In addition, the anti-Chinese sentiment in America is becoming increasingly fierce. Overseas Chinese workers who have been in America for a long time are losing their jobs. Recently, there have been restrictions on Chinese entering the country, so those in the interior who seek work in America are invisibly stopped in their tracks. In this situation, not only are the finances of the Siyi people depleted day by day, but the economy of the entire province is also greatly affected. As for Nanyang, in recent years, due to the low prices of rubber and tin rice and the lack of sales, the number of Nanyang Chinese merchants going bankrupt is increasing day by day. As a result, the number of unemployed Chinese workers in Nanyang is no less than hundreds of thousands, wandering and being expelled back to China by the local government. The situation is so miserable that it is unbearable to witness. The Singapore government, due to the surplus of Chinese workers and fearing that it would affect public order, has issued regulations restricting the entry of Chinese workers, but female guests are not subject to these restrictions. At this time, the silk industry in Shunde and Nanhai counties in Guangdong Province was in decline, and all female workers lost their jobs. As a result, no less than tens of thousands of Shunde female workers went to Nanyang. It was not until the early spring of last year that the prices of Nanyang rubber and tin rice rose, and the declining business seemed to have hopes of recovery. Singapore's limit on the number of Chinese workers entering the country was increased to 4,000 per month. However, due to the simultaneous restriction of production, prosperity has not yet recovered. However, in the midst of this slight turnaround in Nanyang business, Cantonese people flocked to Nanyang again. In addition to the people from Chao'an and Meixian counties who left through Shantou, 4,870 people left the country from Haikou City in half a year (from January to June of this year), and also several hundred people left from Guangzhou City to Hong Kong. Among them, the majority went to Singapore. At this point, there were suddenly more than 100,000 Chinese workers in Nanyang. The slightly developing industry and commerce could not fully accommodate these more than 100,000 people, and the supply of male and female Chinese workers again exceeded demand, with 30-40% unemployed. To prevent this, the Singapore government recently issued new regulations restricting Chinese workers, ordering that from September 1st, the previous limit of 4,000 Chinese workers entering the country will be reduced to 2,500 to adjust the local labor force. Only when industry and commerce develop slightly further will the number of entries be increased as appropriate. (August 15th)

Anhui Province, Tongling County: All Prisoners Break Out of Jail, Seize Dozens of Police Guns, Plot Riot, Security Team Encircle and Attack, Many Killed and Wounded 63

Wuhu Dispatch: In Tongling County, southern Anhui, the government and prison were holding a total of eighty-one inmates, both convicted and awaiting trial. Due to the current hot weather, every day around one or two in the afternoon, they were allowed to fetch water and bathe. On the 17th, at one o'clock in the afternoon, all the prisoners took advantage of this opportunity to riot, first knocking down two guards at the gate, seizing two quick-firing guns, and immediately firing shots as a demonstration. Some of the prisoners in shackles had their shackles removed by their companions. Then, they rushed to the back of the county government, seized over twenty rifles used by the police, and, relying on their perceived strength, planned to rush out of the county government and create disturbances on the streets, causing panic throughout the city. Soon after, the 7th company of the 2nd battalion of the 4th security regiment, newly transferred from Wuhu to garrison in the county, received the news. Led by Company Commander Shi Qicheng, they rushed to the scene and surrounded the county government from the front and rear gates. The prisoners were forced back into the county government's main hall and began to fire in resistance, leading to a fierce battle lasting several hours. The situation throughout the county was extremely tense. Eventually, the prisoners, feeling weak and lacking in courage, some voluntarily returned to their cells, while others escaped by climbing over the walls. The tense situation gradually calmed down and returned to normal. The result was three people killed on the spot, one seriously injured, and several others slightly injured. Eleven people escaped, and most of the seized firearms were recovered. On the security team's side, during the fierce battle, one soldier, Zeng Ruitang, was killed by a bullet. Shao Congxian, Hu Guanghai, and Fu Chuanjie were seriously injured. A passerby, Mr. Jia, was also seriously injured when a stray bullet pierced his cheek. Shao Congxian and Hu Guanghai, who were seriously injured, were sent to Wuhu for medical treatment by boat overnight, but Shao died shortly after landing due to excessive blood loss. Hu was sent to the hospital for treatment. This riot occurred while County Magistrate Qiu Chang was in the countryside surveying the embankments and the security team was being transferred for defense. They attempted to take advantage of the situation, but fortunately, the defense was effective, and the area did not suffer any damage. County Magistrate Qiu has rushed back to the county seat to handle the aftermath and has telegraphed the provincial government and the Second District Commissioner's Office here to report the details of the incident. (18th)

Songjiang: Security Team Deputy Transferred to Garrison 64

Shen Bangda, the deputy of the 12th Security Brigade of Jiangsu Province, has been in Songjiang for several years and has a reputation for military discipline. Recently, he received an order from Director Xiang of the Security Office to be transferred as deputy of the 2nd Brigade, stationed permanently in the provincial capital. His vacancy will be filled by Zhao Zanchen, the deputy of the 13th Brigade. After receiving the order, Shen completed the handover on the 18th. Various institutions held banquets to see him off and presented him with souvenirs. At 11:13 AM on the 19th, he departed by train to the garrison. Brigade Commander Jin Tigan and other officers went to the station to see him off and set off firecrackers to pay their respects.

Wujiang: Tea House Collapse Causes Tragedy 65

At 8:00 AM on the 17th, at the First Building Tea House in the North Port of Beizha Town, our county, while business was bustling, a room on the back of the building suddenly collapsed, causing a room downstairs to collapse as well. The tea guests were caught off guard and unable to escape, resulting in nine injuries. Zhao Jingyun, a barber, died on the spot from a crushed skull. The remaining eight, including Shi Jianshan, sustained injuries of varying degrees of severity and have been sent to Suzhou for treatment. The homeowner, Xia Guanlong, and the tea house owner, Wang Xukui, have been taken into custody by the Public Security Bureau for questioning.

Changshu: Shanghai-Xizhi Road to Extend Northward 66

The Xizhi Highway officially opened to traffic on the 17th, with passenger tickets being sold. On the day of the ceremony, over three thousand guests from Shanghai and Suzhou arrived in Changshu, leaving a very good impression. According to news from the bus station, General Manager Wang Xiaoxiang stated that the company's business policy is to develop the interior, with Changshu as the central hub. Currently, there are plans to extend northward from Changshu, extending the route to Shazhou City and Shiyiwei Port, reaching Nantong. If bridges need to be built across the river, the cost would be high and the project too large, so ferries may be used instead. In the future, north-south transportation along the Yangtze River and the industry and commerce of various counties along the route will be able to develop to their full potential.

Wuxi: Silk Cocoon Prices Soar for Consecutive Days 67

Silk prices have been soaring for consecutive days, with strong exports, raising hopes for the revival of the silk industry. The reason is that European and American countries are using more Chinese silk, while Japan is restricting silkworm rearing, resulting in a decrease in silk cocoon production and sluggish sales of artificial silk. Therefore, this year's silk cocoon market price has soared, marking a new era unseen in recent years. The quality of silk cocoons from the southern route (i.e., Wuxi) is considered the best. The other day, the price of Japanese silk rose to 790 Japanese yen per dan, equivalent to 640 Chinese yuan. Currently, Chinese silk of A grade, 13 to 15 strands, can be sold for around 600 yuan per dan, while 20 and 22 strands can be sold for 530 to 540 yuan per dan. Ordinary silk can also be sold for around 500 yuan. The highest price for cocoons has risen to 135 yuan per dan, with ordinary cocoons at 120 yuan. Thirty-nine silk factories in this county have already started operations.

Changzhou: Construction of Wujiao Road Halted 68

The construction of the Wujin to Jiaoxi highway, contracted out by the highway bus company, has already begun. It is now known that the Construction Department has sent personnel to Changzhou to investigate. Because the road route map and engineering had not been approved by the Department, construction cannot begin. The county has been ordered to halt work immediately and must wait for approval before construction can resume. The county government, upon receiving the order, immediately instructed compliance. As for the extension of the road to Wuxi, technician Shen Zhiyu was dispatched yesterday to conduct surveys. He has now surveyed to the border of Wuxi and will submit the survey results to the Department for approval within days.

Danyang: County Magistrate Bi Resigns and Leaves Danyang 69

Former County Magistrate Bi Jingqian of this county was granted permission by the Provincial Department to resign and officially handed over his duties on August 1st. Various public institutions and local gentry in this county, recognizing County Magistrate Bi's commendable performance during his nearly two-year tenure, initiated a grand farewell gathering and banquet at the County Chamber of Commerce. As County Magistrate Bi's handover was nearing completion, he boarded a car to return home yesterday. From the county government to the train station, memorial banners were posted along the route, and dozens of groups of people lined the streets to see him off. Local public groups and gentry escorted County Magistrate Bi to the train station, where over a thousand people were gathered to bid him farewell. They all raised their hands in salute. As the train departed, military music and firecrackers filled the air. Bi repeatedly nodded from the train window to express his gratitude. The grandeur of the scene was unprecedented in twenty years.

Gaoyou: Thousands of Farmers Demolish County Government 70

The county government of this county has repeatedly received instructions from the Grand Canal Flood Prevention Office and the Provincial Government to expedite the requisition of labor and the accumulation of soil. The county's flood prevention association previously dispatched representatives Ma Junqing, Wang Hongzao, and Ding Fengnian to Huaiyin to meet with Director Xu Dingkang, presenting the difficulties of requisitioning labor and accumulating soil. Director Xu agreed to allow County Magistrate Cao to handle the matter according to local conditions. The office then instructed the county government to provide each cubic foot of soil with a tea and water subsidy of four cents and a subsidy of eight cents for those transported by boat. Work began the other day. However, the laborers had no food, the supervisors were extremely abusive, and the bailiffs privately collected a registration fee of sixty-six copper coins per person. Enduring various hardships and witnessing the arbitrary destruction of their crops, public outrage was ignited. About three thousand farmers, each wielding farm implements, stormed into the county government in the city at 10:00 AM today (the 17th). County Magistrate Cao had gone to Jieshou to inspect the work. The farmers then demolished the police chief's office and the judicial office, destroying all walls, tables, chairs, and equipment. The case files were scattered all over the ground. Important county government officials fled. The judicial secretary, Sun Juexian, and the bailiff, Lu Yunqi, were tied up and severely beaten. Subsequently, they went to the First District Office and the residence of the construction section chief, Jia Fengren, and destroyed everything. As of 8:00 PM, the villagers had not left the city.

Hangzhou: Mogan Mountain Commercial Decline 71

Mogan Mountain is a summer resort in Zhejiang Province. Every summer, many Chinese and foreigners come to the mountain to escape the heat, and hotels and shops all benefit greatly. Due to the decline of the social economy this year, even during the hot summer months, there are very few tourists escaping the heat, and the market is sluggish. The shops in Wukang Road, the busiest commercial area on the mountain, have very few customers, so each shop is complaining and suffering heavy losses. The best ones are barely able to maintain themselves. The number of tourists in all the large and small hotels on the mountain is not as high as in previous years. The newly built houses and villas on the mountain have no takers for rent. The weather has been slightly cooler in recent days, and tourists have been leaving the mountain one after another. The operating revenue of the Mogan Mountain special buses of the Highway Bureau has been greatly affected.

Qiantang River Tide Destroys Residences 72

Since the beginning of autumn this year, the weather has been erratic with frequent wind and rain, and the water level of the Qiantang River has been high. It is now the autumn tide season, and due to the continuous autumn rains, the river tide is more turbulent than in previous years. The water level along the south bank of the river is nearly ten feet high. When the evening tide came the other morning, the houses along the river were submerged in water. Twenty-four shops along the south bank were washed away by the flood, and miscellaneous items were carried away by the water, causing a loss of approximately two thousand yuan. The pontoon bridge of the newly built wharf on the south bank was broken by the flood. A temporary bridge had been erected with wooden machinery at the ferry crossing. Zhang Zili, the director of the Water Conservancy Bureau, made a special trip to inspect the situation and dispatched workers to repair it to facilitate the passage of travelers.

Local News

President Wang Flew to Shanghai from Qingdao Yesterday, Discussing His Resignation Approved by the Central Government, Deciding to Serve the Central Standing Committee in Beijing 73

Central News Agency: After Wang Jingwei, President of the Executive Yuan and Minister of Foreign Affairs, submitted his resignation to the Central Government on the 8th of this month, the Central Government earnestly tried to persuade him to stay. However, Wang's determination to resign was still very firm. Wang arrived in Shanghai by plane from Qingdao yesterday at noon to continue medical treatment and plans to meet with Chairman Chiang Kai-shek in the coming days. The details are as follows:

Arrival in Shanghai Yesterday at Noon

Wang boarded China National Aviation Corporation's Douglas aircraft at 9:20 AM yesterday morning and flew from Qingdao to Shanghai, arriving here at 11:55 AM at noon. He landed at Longhua Airport. Those who went to welcome him included Shanghai Mayor Wu Tiecheng, Secretary-General of the Executive Yuan, Chu Minyi, and Legislative Yuan member Lin Baisheng, among others. After disembarking, Wang went straight to the residence of Zeng at Jierlu (now Jia'er Ai Road) to rest. Those who accompanied Wang to Shanghai yesterday, in addition to Mrs. Wang and her sons and daughters, included Zeng Zhongming, attending physician Luo Guanglin, and secretaries and attendants, totaling more than ten people.

Medical Examination

Wang returned to his private residence on Pushi Road (now Route Tenant de la Tour) at around 1:00 PM yesterday afternoon. He immediately invited Dr. Noel to examine his body and continue treatment. According to Dr. Noel, Wang's body has not yet recovered. Although the fever has subsided, his appetite and spirit have not improved and he still needs a considerable period of recuperation.

Mayor Visits

Wang went to the residence of Zeng on Jierlu again at around 4:00 PM yesterday afternoon and did not return to his private residence to rest until around 7:00 PM in the evening. Mayor Wu visited Wang at around 5:30 PM yesterday afternoon and expressed his condolences. After departing, Mayor Wu told reporters from various newspapers that Wang planned to stay in Shanghai for a short time before entering Beijing. Various parties are making every effort to persuade Wang to stay, but Wang's determination to resign has not been dispelled.

Wang's Remarks

Wang met with reporters from various newspapers at the residence of Zeng on Jierlu yesterday evening. According to his remarks, although my symptoms have subsided, the underlying disease has not been eliminated. Because this treatment was to avoid surgery, the gallstones have not been removed. Therefore, even an ordinary conversation, as long as it exceeds an hour, makes me feel dizzy and my heart race. According to the doctor, I should not work more than four hours each day from now on. However, the work of the Executive Yuan is heavy, and even several four-hour periods are difficult to manage. My body is, of course, of little importance, but if I were to delay national affairs due to my weak body while bearing this heavy responsibility, how would I face the people of the country? This is the reason why I submitted my resignation. Although the Central Government sent a telegram to persuade me to stay, my determination to resign is firm. I have already telegraphed the Central Government again to request resignation. If the Central Government approves my resignation, I will immediately enter Beijing to serve in the Central Standing Committee. I will stay in Shanghai for the time being to continue medical treatment. Chairman Chiang Kai-shek previously sent Zhang Yuejun to Qingdao to meet with me. I telegraphed Chairman Chiang Kai-shek today (the 19th) to inquire about the date and location of the meeting so that we can discuss everything face-to-face.

Sickly and Thin

Wang was wearing a white silk long gown yesterday. His face was thin and unusually pale. It is said that his weight has decreased from 160 pounds to 139 pounds. His spirit was very good, and his gait was healthy. His diet has gradually returned to normal. This is reassuring to the people of the country.

China Industrial Bank and Other Three Banks, Consolidating Our National Finance, Appropriation of Funds to Fill Official Shares of Three Banks, The Ministry of Finance is Currently Reviewing Measures 75

Central News Agency: After the reorganization of the China Industrial Bank, China Merchants Bank, and Siming Bank, the internal strength has become more substantial. At that time, the Ministry of Finance had the idea of appropriating 5 million yuan each to fill the official shares of the three banks in order to enrich the shareholders. According to reporters' inquiries from various parties, this matter is currently being reviewed by the Ministry of Finance. The three banks are all issuing banks. The paid-up capital of the China Industrial Bank is 3,507,400 yuan, and it issues 40 million yuan in convertible notes. The paid-up capital of the China Merchants Bank is 7 million yuan, and it issues approximately 10 million yuan in convertible notes. The paid-up capital of the Siming Bank is 2,250,000 yuan, and it issues more than 10 million yuan in convertible notes. After the reorganization of the three banks, they have become integrated with the Central Bank, the Bank of China, and the Bank of Communications, working together to consolidate our national finance.

After the Ministry of Finance Appropriates Public Bonds to Relief, It is Expected to Pass Through the End of September Safely, Financial Bonds Borrowed by the Money Industry Have Been Repaid One After Another, Few Applications for Interbank Lending from the Central Bank, the Bank of China, and the Bank of Communications 76

New Voice Agency: Since the Ministry of Finance appropriated 25 million yuan in financial bonds in 1935 to relieve the money industry, industry, and commerce and the Central Bank, the Bank of China, and the Bank of Communications handled interbank lending, the financial situation in Shanghai has stabilized, and the revival of industry and commerce is promising. There should be no problems at the end of September. The details are as follows:

Money Industry Recovers and Repays Financial Bonds

After the Ministry appropriated 25 million yuan in financial bonds from 1935 and the Money Industry Supervision Committee was formed to relieve the money industry, each money shop has stabilized after adjustments. They are now repaying the financial bonds to the Ministry of Finance one after another. The rumor that the Ministry is urging the money industry to repay the financial bonds is not true. Similarly, after each money shop has consolidated itself, it is providing relief to industry and commerce, such as extending terms, handling credit loans, and accepting mortgage loans. There is factual proof of this, so industry and commerce have also benefited greatly.

Few Applications for Interbank Lending from Three Banks

After the Central Bank, the Bank of China, and the Bank of Communications jointly raised funds and formed a committee to handle interbank lending before the final settlement of accounts in 1934, it was quite effective. A reporter from New Voice Agency inquired with the three banks yesterday morning and learned that the three banks' interbank lending will continue to be handled. The funds previously lent have been repaid by each bank and money shop one after another. As of yesterday, the amount that had not been repaid was very small. However, there have been no applications for lending recently because the market has stabilized, and there is no need to apply.

Industry and Commerce Expect Mortgage Loans, The Municipal Chamber of Commerce Submits a Request to the Ministry of Finance, Urging Swift Formulation of Measures 77

The Shanghai Municipal Chamber of Commerce submitted a request to the Ministry of Finance yesterday, stating that in order to relieve the market in this city, the Ministry stipulated ten principles for relief loans in the letter Qianzi No. 14130 on April 16, with 15 million yuan as low-interest mortgage loans and 5 million yuan as low-interest credit loans. On July 12, the Ministry issued letter No. 626, stating that the total amount of this mortgage loan of 15 million yuan would be lent by each bank and money shop, and the loan committee would review the report. Now that the credit loan is being processed, the end of September is approaching, and most industries and businesses rely on mortgage loans for turnover, which is particularly important. According to the order, this mortgage loan must be reviewed by the committee before it can be issued. Therefore, the implementation of the mortgage depends on the formulation of the review method. The industry and commerce of this city are eagerly awaiting the realization of this measure, hoping to revitalize the economy. It is appropriate to submit a written request to the Ministry for review and to instruct the association to quickly formulate a method for reviewing and issuing loans and report it to the Ministry for implementation for the public convenience.

Xu Shiying, Telegraphing the Inspection of Disaster Situation in Henan Province, Forty-Seven Disaster Areas in the Province, Losses Approximately 50 Million Yuan, Yanshi City Completely in Ruins, Worse Than War 78

The Shanghai Fundraising Association for Water Disaster Relief in Various Provinces continued to receive a telegram from Xu Shiying yesterday, reporting on the inspection of the flood situation in Yanshi and other counties in Henan Province. The original telegram is extracted as follows: Shanghai Fundraising Association for Water Disaster Relief in Various Provinces, Chairman, Vice-Chairman, Directors, Deputy Directors, Secretary-Generals, Deputy Secretary-Generals, and Gentlemen, Regarding the inspection invited in telegrams Shi Yi and Shi Er, Qian Chen and Fang, the Inspector, traveled south by train from Yanzhou, passing through Hanzhuang and seeing that the water level of the Grand Canal continued to rise. Only the civilians on the east bank of Weishan and Lianghu were busy protecting the banks. At noon, they arrived in Xuzhou and transferred to the Longhai Railway west. The river embankments in Kaocheng, Lanfeng, Kaifeng, and Zhongmu counties in Henan Province were inquired of the personnel sent by the Yellow River Conservancy Commission, who said that there were many major risks, but they were rescued in time. At 9:00 PM, they arrived in Kaifeng and met with Chairman Liu and the officials in charge of the Henan Provincial Water Disaster Relief Association. Since the beginning of the month, Henan Province has experienced continuous rain and mountain torrents, and all large and small rivers have suddenly risen simultaneously. The Yellow River itself overflowed, and Hua County and Fengqiu on the north bank and the Kaifeng, Chenliu, and river beaches on the south bank were submerged. Because the floodwaters of the Yi and Luo rivers could not flow into the Yellow River, the counties along the banks were all affected. Yanshi, located at the confluence of the two rivers, suddenly burst its banks with a water head of three feet, causing the entire county to sink. Gong County, located downstream, was also affected. In addition, the Sha, Ru, Hong, and Ying rivers in the central region also breached their banks, and Xiangyan, and the Cai, Ru, and Nan counties were all flooded. The Bo and Tang rivers in southern Henan overflowed, and the Nanyang, Xinye, Deng County, and Zhenping counties became a swamp. The Xiang River in Xichuan, which originally entered Hubei through Bokou, flowed backward and overflowed, which was inevitable. The entire territory of Danchuan County was flooded, and Huaiyou Xiangling was almost submerged. In northern Henan, the banks of the Qi, Zhang, Jun, and Qin rivers were also affected. It is estimated that there are 47 disaster areas in the province, covering more than 6,000 square kilometers, with estimated losses of more than 50 million yuan. There are 14 counties with total losses exceeding 1 million yuan, and more than 1 million disaster victims. There are many tasks for relief, and after staying overnight in Kaifeng for a brief discussion, Xiao Chen originally planned to transfer to Dongzhuang, Shandong Province, to inspect the Yellow River breach. However, the car journey would still take seven hours, and it has been extremely hot for days, with temperatures above 100 degrees. For the sake of rest, they changed to a special car, and Fang, the Inspector, and Chang Zhizhen, a member of the Henan Provincial Government, traveled together, still along the Longhai Line, to first survey the disaster situation in the west. Passing through Gong County, they saw that all the fields were damaged, and many cultivated lands were buried or destroyed by sand, except for the river banks. It was reported that there were more than 70,000 disaster victims. At noon, they arrived in Yanshi and disembarked to inspect. The entire city had become a ruin, with collapsed houses, pillars, tiles, and wood blocking the roads, and broken walls and dilapidated fences worse than war. Since the flood, 40 days ago, the water in the south of the city was still more than 10 feet deep. The county government has moved to work in a cave in the hills. The 60,000 disaster victims have been displaced and are living in the open, with insufficient clothing and no remaining grass in the fields. The city is desolate and desolate. Zhou, from the United Film Company who came with them, took a film to be shown to the public. The Provincial Water Disaster Association and the Provincial Relief Association have already released 6,000 yuan for emergency relief, and Kong Shen and Cha Rong have donated 2,000 yuan, together with the 2,000 yuan in donations from overseas Chinese carried by Shiying, to transport relief grain, which is being distributed. The sanitation team has also arrived and started working. However, a drop in the bucket is not enough, which is obvious. In the future, it will be necessary to resettle the refugees, prevent major epidemics, relocate the county government, and rebuild houses. At 4:00 PM, they entered Luoyang, and Special Envoy Sheng reported that the situation in Luoyang was slightly better. Overall, the disaster situation in Henan Province cannot be comprehensively alleviated by existing relief efforts. It is hoped that all parties will continue to provide assistance. The details will be reported later. Xu Shiying, Chairman of the Relief Committee, kowtowed. Xiao Yinshi San.

Shipping Industry: Frustration of the Cooperative, Realization of Joint Sharing by Six Companies, Virtual Dissolution of the Cooperative 80

Since all national shipping vessels in this city, adhering to the Ministry's orders, implemented cooperation, a council was organized, and a joint transportation office was planned. After lengthy discussions and investigations by various specialists, it was established through painstaking efforts. The prospects and hopes were boundless. Unexpectedly, with the realization of joint sharing by six companies, the cooperative gradually dissolved virtually. It is truly disheartening to speak of this.

Establishment of the Council

The shipping cooperative, through all Chinese merchant marine shipping companies and the state-run China Merchants Steam Navigation Company, aimed to fundamentally salvage the shipping industry and implement great unity, hoping to reap the initial preparation of equal navigation rights. Therefore, the Ministry of Communications sent personnel to Shanghai to supervise and lead. From June 1st, the shipping cooperative was formally established, attached to 10 Guangdong Road. Due to its grand scale, a council was first established by the state-run and private shipping companies as the cooperative's highest executive body. The state-run China Merchants Steam Navigation Company nominated five council members, and the private shipping companies elected six council members. The council then established various shipping joint transportation offices and a transportation fee committee, etc., placing all ships under a single leadership and management, so as to control routes and openly develop. This was considered an excellent plan.

Failure to Establish Various Offices

According to Article 8 of the cooperative's articles of association, the most important thing under the council was the organization of joint business offices for various routes along the Yangtze River and the sea. Each office would have a director and deputy director, further divided into sections to realize great shipping cooperation. However, soon after the council was established, the cooperative greatly changed its direction. While it was still proceeding in order, a joint sharing association suddenly formed on the Yangtze River route. Participating companies were not limited to national vessels; British, Japanese, and other foreign vessels could participate. Moreover, the tonnage of foreign merchant ships exceeded that of Chinese ships. With the active advancement of joint sharing, the cooperative's affairs were suspended. As a result, the council became an empty title, unable to make progress.

Resignation of Council Members

The council members of the cooperative, seeing that nothing had been done since its establishment, and that all matters that should have been handled could not proceed without funds, requested central assistance at a time when the city was stagnant and the number of idle ships was increasing. However, they were unsuccessful. Consequently, Yu Qiaqing, of the private shipping council, first resigned. Other council members also followed suit, citing a lack of work. The council members elected by the private shipping companies were Yuan [ ], Deng [ ], Bei [ ], Chen Ganqing, and [ ] Bohong, among others. Since the other offices had not been established, there were no issues. However, since Yu's resignation, the other council members have also stopped going to the cooperative to handle affairs. It seems that the cooperative has virtually dissolved.

Fighting Between Overseas Chinese and Locals in Sumatra Calmed, Stopped by Joint Efforts of Dutch East Indies and Chinese Consuls, Overseas Chinese and Locals Now Peaceful, Not Hostile 85

The news of group fighting between overseas Chinese and locals in the Padang, Siantar, and Sibolga areas of Sumatra, Dutch East Indies, due to a soccer game, and the initiation of the conflict, was reported in previous newspapers. According to the Overseas Chinese Federation, since this unfortunate event occurred, the domestic government and public have paid close attention to it. The Overseas Chinese Federation also sent a telegram to inquire, but no reply was received until yesterday. However, private individuals have received letters stating that the matter has been stopped by the joint efforts of Dutch East Indies authorities and Chinese consular officials, who used strong legal measures and informed all overseas Chinese and workers in the Dutch East Indies not to act rashly.
