China-Philippines Tobacco Company Officially Opens Today, The First Sound of Overseas Chinese Returning to the Country to Start a Business 86

The China-Philippines Tobacco Company, founded by prominent overseas Chinese merchants from the Philippines, including Lin Shuyan, Huang Yongkou, Zeng Ruijiao, Gao Zuchuan, Xue Minlao, Lin Jinggu, Lin Zhaopin, and Li Qingquan, is officially opening today. The factory is located at 426 Baoding Road in this city. This can be said to be another successful culmination of the government's policy of encouraging overseas Chinese to return to the country to invest. Historically, the scope of business ventures undertaken by overseas Chinese residing in the Philippines has been limited to the Philippine Islands. Although a small number of overseas Chinese had previously returned to the country, their businesses were mostly concentrated in southern Fujian. However, when Sun Ke, President of the Legislative Yuan, visited the Philippines two years ago, he deeply felt that overseas Chinese were rich in entrepreneurial spirit. He immediately advised them to return to the country to invest and engage in the revitalization of national industries. Later, when Chen Gongbo, Minister of Industry, toured the south last year, he stayed in the Philippine Islands for a week, visited overseas Chinese, and actively encouraged them to return to their motherland and develop industries. The then Consul General to the Philippines, [ ] Guanglin, consistently worked hard to promote the same cause. After this round of vigorous promotion by the government, a group of overseas Chinese in the Philippines decided to raise funds and return to the country to found the China-Philippines Tobacco Company. The capital was quickly raised.

Guaranteeing Patents

Previously, overseas Chinese in the Philippines had established the Philippines Tobacco Company, which invented a type of cigar-style cigarette called "Cigarilla." The American government awarded it a patent, and they wanted to promote it in their home country. However, they were worried about the lack of protection against counterfeiting, so they hesitated. In addition, they produced several other types of cigarettes but did not dare to promote them in their homeland. Later, with the government's guarantee that it would grant exclusive manufacturing and sales rights for this product, the decision to establish a cigarette factory in Shanghai was made. After a period of rapid preparation, the official opening was achieved today. This is the first sound of overseas Chinese returning to the country to start a business. There are currently 150,000 overseas Chinese in the Philippines who are paying close attention to this matter. If it is successful, many more will undoubtedly return to the country to invest in the future, and the national industries of the motherland will be about to unleash a unique splendor.

Manager Selection

Because the Philippines Tobacco Company holds a large share in the China-Philippines Tobacco Company, the managers sent are all highly capable. The general manager is Mr. Lin Zhaopin, who holds a Master's degree in Business Administration from the University of [ ]. He is proficient in finance and advertising and served as the general manager of the Philippines Tobacco Company for ten years. The deputy manager is Mr. Lin Jinggu, also a renowned tobacco magnate in the Philippines, on par with Mr. Lin.

Product Types

The distinguishing feature of the China-Philippines Tobacco Company is machine manufacturing and machine packaging. The machines are all the latest models, and manufacturing is purely scientific. Currently, the products include White House Cigarilla, Hero cigarettes, and Black Girl Petite Luzon sweet cigarettes. The tobacco quality and taste are different. (1) White House Cigarilla is a combination of cigar and cigarette. The raw material is tobacco produced by the company's own tobacco fields in the famous "Isabela" and "Cagayan" tobacco regions of the Philippines and scientifically cured. It is wrapped in American Georgia cigar leaf, with a fragrant aroma. Anyone who usually smokes cigars or cigarettes will surely be satisfied. This product is a new invention, entirely machine-made, clean, and hygienic. Its future popularity can be predicted. (2) Hero cigarettes are made from carefully selected Virginia tobacco leaves, properly blended. The taste is mellow, cool, and refreshing, with all the qualities of imported cigarettes, and fresher. It is also manufactured without human contact, except when the tobacco is manually transported from one machine to another. (3) Black Girl Petite Luzon sweet cigarettes are made from aged and mellow Petite Luzon tobacco leaves produced in the Cagayan region. The cigarettes are 30% larger than ordinary cigarettes. The selling prices of the above three products are all low. The White House and Black Girl brands are especially inexpensive, so that people from all walks of life can enjoy high-quality cigarettes at a very low price.

Business Policy

According to General Manager Lin Zhaopin, the selling price is not the primary concern. He said, "The profit per pack of cigarettes of our company is certainly not as high as that of other cigarette factories. However, we intend to achieve success through small profits and large sales. From the very beginning, our company will focus on quality, and our future success will depend solely on superior quality."

Tour Return Tickets Must Have Return Section Date Stamped 87

The Shanghai-Nanjing and Shanghai-Hangzhou-Ningbo Railway Administration has decided that from August 21st of this year (i.e., tomorrow), all passengers using the return section of tour return tickets must have the date stamped by the ticket office before boarding the train, otherwise the ticket will be invalid. July Traffic Report: Number of People Killed by Cars 88

According to the Shanghai Municipal Council Police Department's July traffic report, a total of 2,308 cases of violations of traffic regulations were reported during the month, of which 706 cases were criminally prosecuted in court, including 607 cases involving Chinese and 99 cases involving foreigners. The remaining cases that were not prosecuted were given warnings or had their offenses recorded, depending on the severity of the offense and their nationality. During the month, 1,712 rickshaw pullers were detained by the Central and Zhabei police stations for violating traffic regulations. Three private rickshaw pullers had their licenses revoked for soliciting business. There were 78 cases of taxi drivers overusing their horns that were dealt with. Four taxi drivers had their licenses revoked for repeated offenses. There were 836 traffic accidents during the month, including 92 cases of property damage and personal injury (no deaths), 473 cases of property damage, 271 cases of personal injury (six deaths).

Shanghai-Nanjing and Shanghai-Hangzhou-Ningbo Railway Administration Strictly Prohibits Foremen from Extorting Fees Under the Guise of Festive Gifts, All Levels of Staff Should Refuse Gifts 89

The Shanghai-Nanjing and Shanghai-Hangzhou-Ningbo Railway Administration issued instructions to various departments stating: "It has been reported that there are still unscrupulous foremen on this railway who are extorting money from the workers under their command in the name of sending gifts during the three major festivals, which is truly hateful. It is hereby strictly ordered to eradicate this practice, and personnel will be dispatched to conduct secret investigations at any time and place. Once discovered, in addition to immediately dismissing the foreman, his direct superiors shall also be subject to severe disciplinary action. Furthermore, all levels of staff should refuse gifts to prevent the gradual spread of bribery. This is hereby ordered."

Autopsy of Corpse Murdered in Luhang District, One Suspect Apprehended 94

A male corpse murdered by someone was found on the bank of the Xiaobang in Chenjiazhai, Shuzigou, Beicai, Luhang District, Pudong the day before yesterday at dawn. Fishing nets and baskets were left next to the corpse, indicating that he was stealing fish and shrimp, was spotted by someone, and was murdered. Someone reported the incident to the Dongcai police station, which instructed the Baojia, Chen Yuetang, to report it to the District Court Prosecutor's Office for an autopsy. All details have been reported in this newspaper. It has been learned that the court dispatched Prosecutor Xiao Jinying, along with the coroner, to Pudong yesterday afternoon to conduct an autopsy. The autopsy revealed that the deceased was about thirty years old, wearing a blue cloth short shirt and pants, bald, barefoot, and had countless axe wounds to his head, which was shattered, resembling a split pomegranate, with brain matter and blood flowing everywhere. The situation was particularly tragic, and he died from his injuries. A coroner's report was filled out. As there were no relatives to identify the body, it was ordered to be placed in a coffin by the [ ] Hall, pending the arrest and punishment of the murderer. An investigation revealed that the fish and shrimp in the Xiaobang were raised by Chen, a villager from Chenjiazhai. Recently, petty thieves have frequently laid nets to steal. Therefore, Chen hated them to the bone because the number of fish and shrimp purchased annually did not make up. Even if the fish and shrimp were caught and sold in the market, it would not be worth it. So, he would get up and secretly observe at night, wanting to catch them at any cost. After the incident, the Gouwei police station sent police officers to investigate the murderer in all directions and apprehended Chen. Because the short shirt he was wearing was covered in blood stains, it was suspicious. He was taken to the police station for interrogation. Although Chen denied it, the suspicion was great. It was ordered to be held in custody and transferred to the court for further investigation.

Subsequently, the plaintiff Youming testified in detail about being forced to take photos with Wang Amei and forced to sign IOUs. Zhang Ayuan was a friend of the monk. He wanted to borrow money but could not, so he thought of this method. At that time, she went into the room but did not know if Qiu Zhongyuan went there. Wang Amei testified that Zhang Ayuan came up with the idea to defraud money. She received 100 yuan afterwards. At this point, the court, needing to investigate further, adjourned the hearing to the 23rd. The defendants were returned to custody. However, Qiu Zhongyuan presented a request to be transferred to the detention center because he was coughing up blood in custody. District Branch Representatives of Citizens' Association Offer Telephone Opinions, Requesting Attention to User Interests 100

The Shanghai Telephone Company of the Shanghai International Settlement has repeatedly increased its rates, opposed by various public organizations throughout the city. The Municipal Council has temporarily agreed to a rate increase of 12.5% and established a research committee. Foreign committee members have successively arrived in Shanghai. The First District Branch of the Citizens' Association of the Special District, which has been the most vocal in opposing telephone rate increases, has specifically appointed standing committee members Xu Meiqing and Zhuang Zhihe to visit Hu Ruixiang, the Chinese member of the committee, today. They will request that attention be paid to the interests of users to embody the true spirit of public utilities and facilitate transportation. They will also solemnly state the reasons for their opposition for the committee's consideration. A summary is as follows: (1) Shanghai's situation has deteriorated to an extreme point. Few businesses can barely maintain operations. Further increasing their burden would be difficult to bear. The Shanghai Telephone Company already has profits and performs better than ordinary businesses. It should share the hardships with users and should not necessarily achieve its budgetary goals by raising prices again. (2) Telephones are a public utility, with the purpose of benefiting the public. Profits should be limited. No matter what country, there is no regulation that public utilities must guarantee a certain level of profit. Why does the Shanghai Telephone Company have such a harsh demand, and why must the Municipal Council allow it? (3) In terms of progress, it is difficult for general users to truly understand the actual situation of the Shanghai Telephone Company's profits and losses before they have the opportunity to accurately understand its actual contents. It is also difficult to believe the company's need to increase prices. (4) The Shanghai Telephone Company has declared that it needs to increase prices due to excessive capital investment and huge expenditures. However, according to commercial practice, the higher the price, the more difficult it is to sell. It is better to have small profits and quick turnover for easy promotion. The company only knows how to spend money on advertising and cannot see through society. It is clumsy to seek profit by reducing prices. As for expenditures, it is not necessarily impossible to reduce them. (5) The method of calculating the price increase by call is even more limitless. According to the results of the association's investigation of the actual usage of various users, it will exceed the original price by more than two or three times. Although the Municipal Council has not yet approved it, even allowing an increase of 12.5% is not something that users can afford.

Special District Rickshaw Pullers Gathered Yesterday to Take Over the Mutual Aid Society, and Requested the Municipal Chamber of Commerce and Taxpayers' Association to Attend as Directors; Authorities Persuaded Them to Postpone the Takeover for One Week 102

According to Xin Sheng She, Special District rickshaw pullers requested the publication of the mutual aid society's accounts. They mass petitioned yesterday, preparing to take over. The authorities persuaded them to stop. Details are as follows:

District Assembly

The rickshaw pullers of the Special District pay a monthly membership fee of 15,000 yuan to the mutual aid society. To date, they have paid a total of 195,000 yuan. They have repeatedly requested the publication of accounts but have not been accepted. Therefore, at eight o'clock yesterday, the rickshaw pullers gathered in five districts (Pudong in Yangshupu, Puxi and Pubei in Jinling Road, Puzhong in Lujiawan, and Punan in Lujiabang Road), totaling more than 5,000 people, preparing to take over the mutual aid society in Jiaxing Road.

Request for Protection

Beforehand, the rickshaw pullers, in order to request protection from the authorities, specifically sent Zhu Fengxiang, chairman of the Rickshaw Pullers Association, and executive committee members Zhu Richang, Dai Rugui, Zhou Hanqing, Lu Deguang, and Sun Shihe, a total of six people, to the Central Police Station to request protection and announced the reasons: (1) Publish the accounts, (2) Announce the procedures for the election of new directors of the mutual aid society, (3) Rickshaw puller directors should be recognized, (4) If the staff members are too busy with association affairs to publish the accounts, please suspend work for a few days to allow for proper reorganization. Chief Inspector Yao Zengmo received them and advised the rickshaw pullers to delay the action and wait for discussion with Deputy Chief Inspector Asmus to seek a proper solution.

Petitions Everywhere

At nine o'clock, directors Cang Gongwen, Xu Zhulin, and standing committee members Xu Buhua, Li Yourong, Bian Weilian, You Muqing, and Ma Taizhi, a total of seven people, first went to the residence of Chinese Director Yu Qiaqing in Haining Road. Because Yu was not present, they went to Foch Road, but he had already gone out. Then they presented a letter to the Sanbei Company, asking Yu to serve as the chairman of the mutual aid society and be responsible for convening a new board of directors. They did not meet him either. Then they sent Xu Zhucai, Lu Deqing, and Cang Gongwen to the Taxpayers' Chinese Association to report the situation and request the appointment of one person each from the Municipal Chamber of Commerce and the Taxpayers' Association to attend as a director of the mutual aid society. Secretary Tao Leqin received them and promised to ask for instructions and handle it.

Postponed Takeover

When the rickshaw puller representatives were petitioning in separate directions, more than 700 rickshaw pullers in Pudong District went to various locations such as Jiaxing Road and Dixiwei Road to wait for news. If there were no satisfactory results, they prepared to take over the mutual aid society. The Jiaxing Road Police Station, upon receiving the report, sent a large number of detectives to maintain order. Until 1:00 PM, the petition representatives returned to report. It was resolved to respect the mediators' wishes and delay the takeover for one week.

Reasons for Takeover

The reasons why the rickshaw pullers prepared to take over the mutual aid society yesterday were that the Municipal Council did not recognize the mutual aid society as an affiliated organization. Repeated direct negotiations had no results. The Taxpayers' Chinese Association replied to the Rickshaw Pullers' Association, saying: "We have received a reply from the Public Concession Municipal Council, a letter dated August 6th regarding the transfer of a letter from the Public Rickshaw Pullers' Association. The Rickshaw Pullers' Mutual Aid Society has its own organization and is not under the jurisdiction of the Municipal Council. If there are any letters regarding this issue, it is best to send them directly to the Mutual Aid Society."

The Xiang Yixing Kidnapping Case: A Glimpse of the Criminal Confessions; Taking a Monk's Robe as Evidence; Presenting a Statement Expressing Willingness to Pay Ransom; Involving a Female Worker at a Pharmaceutical Factory 108

The kidnapping of Xiang Yixing, owner of a sand-turning factory on Hongnan Mountain Road in Zhabei, and the details of the subsequent investigation have been repeatedly reported. Now, the confessions of the captured criminals in this case are detailed as follows:

(1) Zhou Shi (i.e., Miss Shi) states: 26 years old, from Ningbo, residing at No. 7 Yuande Lane, Julai Da Road. I practiced Daoism in the Yixinlu Buddhist hall built by my master (referring to Xiang Yixing). 500,000 yuan

to redeem him. He also brought a monk's robe worn by my master, a white short shirt, as proof. I took the robe to the Xiang family, and they gave me 200 yuan in banknotes to contact Chen. Guo Huatang Sues His Stepmother and Others for Encroachment, Misappropriating Seals to Withdraw Public Funds, and Selling HSBC Shares 109

Guo Zibin, a wealthy Chaozhou merchant in Shanghai, founded the Hongzhang Cotton Mill and other industries, possessing assets of millions. His late wife, Zheng, bore him two sons, the eldest named Huatang and the second named Futing. His second wife, Yao, bore him a son named Liangfu. Wang bore him a son named Wenjun. Yang had no children. Finally, he married Fang, who bore him a son named Wenzhong. Because Guo had many children, he had already divided all his assets among his children in his will before his death and allocated a portion of his assets to serve as public assets, and another portion was allocated to charitable causes. On August 21, 1932, Guo Zibin passed away due to illness. The funeral was extremely extravagant at the time. Recently, Guo Huatang, the eldest son of Zibin, suddenly discovered that his stepmother Fang and his brother Futing had misappropriated his private seals, withdrew huge amounts of public funds from the Xinyu Money Exchange, and sold more than 100 HSBC shares. Considering this to be encroachment and breach of trust, he then hired lawyer Ge Ci Dong to file a complaint with the criminal court of the First Special District Court against Fang and Guo Futing. Yesterday, Judge Feng Shide opened the first criminal court for a continued hearing. Guo Fang hired lawyers Hua Maosheng and Jiang Yiping. Guo Futing hired lawyer Chen Tingrui for defense. Guo Fang claimed that after Zibin's death, a funeral committee was organized to hold a 100-day funeral. At that time, due to the lack of cash, HSBC shares were mortgaged to the Xinyu Money Exchange to open a credit line account. The funds used were jointly sealed by the plaintiff and his five brothers, and all the funds used were recorded in the account books. She then presented the public account books and the total expenses after Zibin's death as proof. However, Guo Huatang claimed that he had never seen these two account books. The court, with the facts clear, then had lawyer Ge and lawyers Chen Tingrui and Hua Maosheng debate each other. Judge Feng instructed to await a scheduled sentencing.

A Factory Manufacturing Counterfeit Coins Uncovered in Pudong; Two Male and Female Criminals Arrested; Hundreds of Counterfeit Coins Confiscated 110

Captain Wang of the Detective Squad of the Pudong Public Security Bureau learned that someone was privately manufacturing counterfeit coins in a thatched hut at No. 88 behind Qingnianhui New Village. Around 10 p.m. the night before, he ordered squad leader Chen Jinshan to lead detectives Zhang Xixiang, Jinsheng, Jiang Binru, and others to the address, where they arrested the main criminal, Pan Fangcun from Chongming, and a female criminal, Pan Xi. They confiscated a coil of copper wire, a pair of scissors, a rubber stamp, a tank of silver liquid, thirteen nameplate models, two dry cells, half a small box of plaster powder, two files, and one hundred finished counterfeit coins. The witnesses were also brought to the bureau. After Director Zhang interrogated them, he ordered them to be sent to the headquarters for interrogation.

Failing to Find Work, Unable to Return Home, Ashamed and Indignant, He Committed Suicide by Taking Poison; Wang Shou Kang's Plight is Pitiful 111

Wang Shou Kang, a 25-year-old from Shaoxing, used to work in a cloth shop in Hangzhou. He was dismissed due to an incident. A few days ago, he came to Shanghai and stayed with his cousin for a few days. Later, his cousin gave him three yuan to return to his hometown, instructing him to invite him back when the opportunity arises. After Wang said goodbye, he did not return. On the 10th day, he went alone to Room 22 of the Haitongchun Inn in Yude Lane, Yunnan Road. Because he failed to find work in Shanghai and was ashamed to return home, he thought

again and again

and finally had the idea of dying. He secretly took raw opium and committed suicide. At six o'clock the next morning, the tea waiter heard vomiting from the room and knew something was wrong. He opened the door and saw that the Wang traveler was lying on the bed, pale and breathless. He quickly sent him to Renji Hospital for treatment.

Overseas, a Sailboat Hit a Reef and Sank; A Case of Bandits Kidnapping 112

A sailor from Ningbo who arrived in Shanghai yesterday said that in the waters of Changbingzui, Southeast Zhitou, in the seventh district of Zhenhai, Ningbo, a large sailboat was hit by waves and sank after hitting a reef. Three crew members and unknown thugs escaped by swimming. According to the owner of the sailboat, Jia Duixin, the ship set sail from Zhongli Port, Liuheng, Dinghai on the 9th of this month, originally bound for Ningbo. On the way, six people with wooden guns boarded the ship and forced the captain to sail the ship to Zhitou. In the Jiang area, a farmer named Shi Baoben was kidnapped by the bandits and a huge ransom was demanded. He was first taken to the Lingdun area of Zhongli Bay. One of the bandits was familiar with the victim. Baoben secretly negotiated an escape with the bandit, but the other bandits found out. At that time, the bandits tore up Shi Baoben. Fearing accidents, they fled together, boarded this sailboat, and forced it to sail to Zhitouyang. Unexpectedly, they encountered a storm and hit a reef at Changbingzui, and the six bandits escaped.

Zhang Jintao and Others Accused of Defamation 116

Lawyer Long Wenxuan and Yinghui were entrusted on May 1 of this year to handle the liquidation of the Laohetai Restaurant in Chenjiazhai, Pudong. On May 3, Zhang Jintao, the owner of the Xiangtai Meat Shop on Beihutang Road, Pudong, and Ye Hengshao, the owner of the Fangxintai Meat Shop, posted a notice on the restaurant's door panel, "It is stated that the owner of the Laohedong Restaurant stole and transported items and fled. Entrusted a lawyer to liquidate, there are acts of collusion and deception." A letter was sent to warn, but it was ignored. Therefore, according to Article 310, Paragraph 2 of the Criminal Law, the crime of defamation was filed against Zhang and Ye with the criminal court of the Shanghai District Court. The court approved the summons to open the trial at 8 a.m. on the 9th of this month. The defendant was not present, only the defense attorney arrived in court to change the date to 11 a.m. on the 19th of this month. Judge Tan of the criminal court opened the tenth court to continue the trial. Plaintiff Long Wenxuan and his agent, lawyer Fang, defendants Zhang Jintao and Ye Hengshao and their defense attorney, Gu Jirong, appeared in court. Although the defendants denied posting the notice and harming reputation, Judge Tan verified the handwriting and other evidence in court and considered that the previous court should not have resisted the summons and failed to appear. He ruled in court that the two defendants would be released on bail and the witnesses would be summoned to court for questioning. At that time, the defendants' defense attorney, Gu Jirong, requested that they be exempted from bail, but the court refused.

Letters to the Editor 127

To the Esteemed Editor of Shen Bao,

With utmost respect, I write to inform you that upon reading the publication news on the fourth page of today's (August 19th) edition of your esteemed newspaper, it stated that an article by Zhang from the North was published in the "New Shanghai Cartoon." I believe this is a misunderstanding based on rumors. I hope you will correct it. I would be immensely grateful. With best wishes.

Sincerely,

Zhang Ziping of the North, August 19th

To the Esteemed Editor of Shen Bao,

Since the beginning of summer, the medical and pharmaceutical communities of Pudong, for the sake of the health of the poor, have jointly organized the Pudong Poor People's Clinic and Dispensary within the Yangjing Temple. The medical and pharmaceutical communities both embrace the spirit of self-sacrifice and service to society, seeking happiness for the poor. Only a small fee of one silver dollar is collected to cover the cost of medicine. All dispensing procedures involve the dispensary issuing vouchers for the poor to collect medicine from various pharmacies, without any charge whatsoever. The poor benefit greatly, and everyone praises this initiative.

Recently, it has come to our attention that unscrupulous individuals are exploiting the name of our organization to solicit donations externally, undermining this charitable cause. This is truly detestable. We deeply fear that outsiders may be deceived. Therefore, we have specially sent a letter to the Pudong Public Security Bureau, instructing them to pay close attention to investigating these matters at any time. We also respectfully request that you, sir, grant us a small space in the "Letters to the Editor" column of your esteemed newspaper to publish this notice and clarify the facts. We would be immensely grateful.

Respectfully yours,

Pudong Public Clinic and Dispensary for the Poor, August 19th

Conclusion of the Yong'an Silver Company Case - Yesterday, Judge Xiao renewed the trial. Lin Kanghou's statements were all "I don't know." Shen Zufu, Wang Yongxin, etc., all had arrest warrants issued.

The lawsuit has been ongoing for over half a year. The court summons has been issued more than ten times. Seventeen directors and managers of the bankrupt Yong'an Silver Company were successively sued by 27 creditor households for fraud, embezzlement, and breach of trust. Yesterday afternoon, Judge Xiao Xiefen of the First Special District Local Court opened the third court session. Only two defendants were present: Lin Kanghou, chairman of the National Federation of Commerce and secretary-general of the Bankers' Association, who had previously provided a guarantee of 10,000 yuan, and Ou Jiancheng, director and general manager of the company, who had provided a guarantee of 30,000 yuan. The remaining individuals who were appointed as directors or served as managers and assistant managers, including Deng Jinghuan, Wang Jiazhen, Li Du, Zhang Zilian, Qian Youju, Ye Hancheng, Lin Qiuhu, Peng Zhenhui, Jiang Qi, Gu Chuntao, Shen Zufu, Luo Huafang, Wang Yongxin, and Dai Kechang, were all absent. Most of the plaintiffs were represented by lawyers. The judge originally presiding over the case was Wu Zehan. Now, due to Judge Wu's transfer to another court, the vacancy has been filled by Judge Xiao Xiefen. In order to understand the entire case, Judge Xiao announced a renewed trial after the court session began. He also instructed the lawyers representing both the plaintiffs and defendants that there are currently 14 outstanding private prosecutions against the defendants, excluding those that have already been withdrawn or concluded. However, since the implementation of the new Criminal Procedure Law, such private prosecution cases cannot be withdrawn even if the parties reach an out-of-court settlement. Therefore, regardless of whether the cases have been settled out of court, they will still proceed according to the law. Subsequently, each plaintiff or their representative lawyer was questioned about the details of the charges and the amount of money embezzled, and evidence such as deposit books and deposit slips was examined. Most of the deposits were of a fixed, current, or transactional nature. However, the circumstances of the claims pursued by Feng Shunqing and a middle-aged woman were slightly different. According to Feng's lawyer, the amount embezzled from Feng, in addition to a small portion of deposits, consisted of profits earned from entrusting the company to buy large bars of silver and the deposit of security deposits. However, according to defendant Ou Jiancheng, Feng was originally a shareholder. The amount of shares he subscribed for was initially 30,000, but later reduced to 10,000. However, he only paid 3,000 yuan and then wanted to renege on his subscription. Therefore, the remaining 7,000 yuan of share capital was never paid, affecting the progress of other subscribers' payments. Furthermore, all other profits were from his purchase of large bars of silver, and there was no deposit. The defendant could not be held liable for fraud. As for the middle-aged woman, she had mortgaged a total of 30,000 yuan of treasury bonds and public bonds to the company for 11,000 yuan in cash for a term of three months. However, before the redemption period arrived, the company went out of business. Although the period for redemption had arrived when the company resumed business, the company had privately sold the collateral without authorization, so when the woman prepared funds for redemption, she was not able to have the items returned. During the court hearing, defendants Ou Jiancheng and Lin Kanghou were interrogated. Lin replied to every question with "I don't know." Ou did not have much objection to the amounts pursued by the plaintiffs. The court further questioned Ou as to why the company only registered in the United States and did not apply for registration with the Ministry of Finance of the country, given that it had advertised a capital of one million. After Ou's defense, the debate began. Some plaintiffs declared that they would withdraw the prosecution against Lin Kanghou, while others argued that since Lin served as a director, he should be held jointly liable with Ou for fraud. After the lawyers for Ou and Lin presented their defenses, Judge Xiao issued arrest warrants for defendants Shen Zufu and Wang Yongxin, who had consistently failed to appear. The plaintiffs were instructed to apprehend them. For defendants whose addresses were unknown and could not be served, public notice was given. Lin and Ou were each released on their original bail, and a date was set for sentencing.

(9) Regarding whether athletes selected by the martial arts halls in various provinces and cities can directly register with this committee, it was resolved that they should still report to the administrative organs of their respective units for submission to the committee.

(11) Regarding the proposal to appoint a president of the Games, it was resolved to appoint Minister Wang Shijie as the president of the Games and submit it for retroactive recognition at the second plenary meeting of this committee.

Sports Masterpiece - "Gentle Exercise" Published Today - Compiled by Ms. Zhang Huilan and Ms. Sun Zhenghe 138

The Diligent Bookstore at 391 Rue du Père Robert, French Concession, has specially invited experts Zhang Huilan and Sun Zhenghe, former professors of the Department of Physical Education at the Central University and current professors of the Department of Physical Education at the Hebei Provincial Women's Normal School, to compile the book "Gentle Exercise". The book has already been published. The outline is as follows: Chapter 1 Posture, Section 1 Good Posture, Section 2 Bad Posture, Section 3 Detailed Description of the Posture of Various Parts of the Body, Chapter 2, Section 1 Organization and Management, Section 2 Selection of Teaching Materials, Section 3 Arousal of Interest, Section 4 Correction Methods, Chapter 3 Correction Methods for Other Defects Chapter 4 Examples of Teaching Materials, Section 1 Teaching Materials for Each Subject (16 Lessons) Section 2 Teaching Materials for Various Sports, Section 3 Games, Section 4 Dance, each chapter is divided into sections, and each section is subdivided into points. It is extremely detailed and contains more than 100 illustrations, which are even more valuable. It is suitable for general universities, middle schools, primary schools, the public, and families. The whole book is paperback and printed on Swedish paper. The price is one yuan, with a special price of 10% off. The bureau's retail department at 277 Four Ma Road, British Concession, also sells at the same price.

Educational News

This City's Year 24 Implementation Plan for Compulsory Education Requires a Total Annual Expenditure of Over 180,000 Yuan to Gradually Enable Out-of-School Children to Attend School 139

It is estimated that there are approximately 70,000 out-of-school children in this city's district. The Municipal Education Bureau has formulated a compulsory education implementation plan to be implemented starting in Year 24. A Compulsory Education Committee has been organized to carry out the plan. The implementation plan is excerpted as follows:

A. Implementation Methods

It is estimated that there are approximately 70,000 out-of-school children in this city's district (excluding the Special District). Starting in Year 24, the first phase of compulsory education will be implemented, with approximately 14,000 (one-fifth of the total) out-of-school children required to be enabled to attend school each year. In accordance with the provisions of the Provisional Outline of Compulsory Education Implementation Measures, the following matters shall be implemented:

Short-Term Elementary Schools

(1) Establish one-year short-term elementary schools and attached short-term elementary school classes. Starting in Year 24, it is planned to establish 20 short-term elementary schools, each with morning, noon, and evening classes, and 90 short-term elementary school classes attached to ordinary elementary schools, totaling 150 classes. Each class will enroll 50 students, accommodating a total of 7,500 students. The monthly recurring expenses for each short-term elementary school are estimated at 80 yuan, totaling 19,200 yuan per year. The start-up cost for each school is estimated at 200 yuan, totaling 4,000 yuan. The monthly recurring expenses for each attached short-term elementary school class are estimated at 24 yuan, totaling 25,920 yuan per year. The cost of books and supplies is estimated at 1 yuan per student per year, totaling 7,500 yuan. The total cost is 56,620 yuan in silver.

Promoting Junior Elementary Schools

(1) Promote junior elementary schools. In Year 24, it is planned to add six elementary schools, such as restoring Lu Bin Elementary School at Longhua New Village Elementary School, establishing an elementary school on land donated by Jiang Zuozhou in Yangjing District, adding an elementary school at Yangshupu where Wang Zengyou built school buildings, and incorporating the private Anguo Dadongxi Compulsory Elementary School as a municipal school. It is planned to operate single-grade classes in two schools, two-grade classes in one school, and three-grade classes in three schools, totaling 13 grades, accommodating 650 students. The monthly expenses for a single-grade class are 100 yuan, for a two-grade class 160 yuan, and for a three-grade class 240 yuan, totaling 12,960 yuan per year. The start-up cost is 200 yuan per grade, totaling 2,600 yuan. The total cost is 15,560 yuan in silver.

Expanding School Grades

(3) Expanding the grades of existing elementary schools. In Year 23, there were a total of 44,286 elementary school students in the city, with 798 grades, averaging 55.5 students per grade, which is already extremely crowded. In practice, it is impossible to further expand the capacity of existing grades. In Year 24, it is planned to add 40 grades to existing grades, with each grade accommodating 50 students, totaling 2,000 students. The monthly recurring expenses for each grade are approximately 80 yuan, totaling 38,400 yuan per year. The start-up cost is 100 yuan per grade, totaling 8,000 yuan. The total cost is 46,400 yuan in silver.

Implementing a Two-Shift System

(4) Vigorously implement a two-shift system. This city has had a four-grade two-shift system, but its implementation has been hindered. Therefore, it was only piloted in schools such as He'an. Starting in Year 24, it is planned to add 36 grades, with each grade accommodating 100 students, totaling 3,600 students. The monthly recurring expenses for each grade are approximately 100 yuan, totaling 43,200 yuan per year. The start-up cost is 200 yuan per grade, totaling 7,200 yuan. The total cost is 50,400 yuan in silver.

Improving Private Schools

(5) Improving private schools. According to a survey conducted by dispatched personnel, approximately 250 private schools in the city have registered with the bureau. The shortcomings of private schools are: (1) School buildings are not sanitary enough; (2) Equipment is too simple; (3) Teachers' knowledge is too low. Each school will be given a subsidy of 20 yuan per year to expand equipment, renovate school buildings, purchase reference books, and allow teachers to visit nearby excellent schools for observation. This totals 5,000 yuan per year. In addition, the establishment of a private school teacher training class requires 3,580 yuan, totaling 8,580 yuan in silver.

Mobile Education

(6) Piloting mobile education. Pilot mobile education vehicles will go deep into rural areas to work. It is planned to first establish five vehicles for pilot operation. If each vehicle teaches 50 students, 350 students can be taught. Each vehicle will be responsible for one teacher, with a provisional monthly salary of 30 yuan, totaling 1,800 yuan per year. Each vehicle will employ one driver, with a monthly salary of 16 yuan, totaling 720 yuan per year, totaling 2,520 yuan. The manufacturing cost for each vehicle is approximately 50 yuan, totaling 250 yuan. The total cost is 2,770 yuan in silver. The total recurring expenses for the implementation of compulsory education in this city in Year 24 are 147,200 yuan, and the temporary expenses are 33,130 yuan, totaling 180,330 yuan.

B. Teachers

(1) Give priority to employing graduates from this year's municipal and registered private normal schools and senior high school normal departments; (2) Select and hire qualified personnel registered with this bureau; (3) If insufficient, establish teacher training classes or hold public examinations for recruitment.

C. School Buildings and Equipment

(1) Fully utilize the remaining rooms of existing school buildings; (2) Utilize public places such as public offices, ancestral halls, and other public venues; (3) When necessary, rent private houses, but prioritize those with low rents and suitable use; (4) Utilize the original equipment of various schools. New equipment should be simple and practical in principle.

The Ministry of Education Formulates Measures for the Management of Compulsory Education Funds and Orders All Education Bureaus to Comply 140

(Nanjing, 19th dispatch) The central government has subsidized 2.4 million yuan for compulsory education funds to various provinces, and the distribution will begin in July. In order to supervise the custody and use of the funds, the Ministry of Education has specially formulated four outlines for the management of compulsory education funds in various provinces and cities, and ordered all education bureaus to comply. The main points of the outlines are: (1) A designated bank should be specified for special deposit; (2) No transfer for other purposes is allowed; (3) The provincial and municipal compulsory education committees should report the amount of income and expenditure to the Ministry for record each month; (4) If non-compliance is found, the central government subsidy may be suspended. The Ministry of Education may announce over one hundred words on the 20th, and instruct all provincial and municipal education bureaus to implement.

The friendship between the two of them is very deep; even if someone laughs at Little Qiao for being affectionate to Little Mei, he will not stop because of it. Tidbits 150

— (Qiu Lang)

Society often uses the names of objects to scold people, to show frivolousness and contempt. In fact, the objects referred to are beneficial to us, so why despise them? A brief description is given below.

Candle People often call those who are not very clever in doing things or are often deceived by others "candles"! In fact, the candle itself always sacrifices its entire life, giving light and convenience to others. We should admire its spirit of self-sacrifice and benefiting others, but society insults it instead, I don't know what the reason is?

Rice Bucket People often call those who are naturally mediocre or not very sensible "rice buckets"! It must be known that a rice bucket is used to hold three meals of porridge and rice for people to eat. For the sake of survival, no one can do without food and drink for a day. Then the rice bucket has great achievements for the crowd, so why despise it?

Western-style Houses and Bungalows 151

— Wei Jing

That was a wasteland. Three years ago, it was still a rubble field. According to the older people, that rubble field used to be a large house. Because the descendants in the large house declined, it was never rebuilt after a fire.

In the year three years ago, the neighbors were spreading the news that the wasteland had been sold. One owner bought the entire square, measuring more than four mu of land. One owner bought the narrow strip on the southeast corner, measuring more than eight fen and seven li of land.

A few days later, the two owners successively built houses on the newly bought land. On the more than four mu of land, a Spanish-style Western house was built. There were lawns around, as well as well-arranged flowers and trees. The construction project took a full eight months to complete. But the house built on the narrow strip of land was completed in only two months, because this family's house was a row of nine-bay tile bungalows. On all the remaining land, the rubble was just leveled a little, and everything was simple.

After the houses of the two families were built, they successively moved in. The family living in the Western-style house was said to be involved in politics, so the owner never paid attention to anyone when going in and out. Even the servants were somewhat indifferent to the neighbors. But the family living in the bungalow, the foreman's family, was very friendly and often interacted with the neighbors.

Last year, the owner of the Western-style house did not know what he had done wrong, lost his official position, and died in a hurry. It was said that he was still in debt after his death, so the Western-style house was immediately transferred to the real estate company. At the same time! The family living in the bungalow, because they were preparing to marry a daughter-in-law, added two rooms to the remaining land.

For a time, the neighbors looked at the Western-style house, looked at the bungalow, and would sigh slightly.

The Metropolis at Dusk 152

— Zhu Shoutong

The sun's weak, gentle rays slant across the rooftops and eaves of the city, retaining only their golden hue, lacking the fierce intensity of midday.

The pedestrians on the streets are especially crowded, adding to the bustling atmosphere. The red and green traffic lights change like the blinking of an eye. The traffic police, directing traffic, blow their whistles, the "dee-loo," "dee-loo" sounds constantly vibrating through the air.

"Ke-dang," "ke-dang," the trams run one after another, and at each stop, a batch of passengers surges out, followed by another batch挤挤on, so that there is no space to put a foot down inside the carriages, but the platforms are still full of people waiting. Newspaper boys, shouting their sales pitches like reciting familiar phrases, weave through the crowds. Seeing a tram approaching, they swarm forward, holding out evening papers from the windows, shouting with extra vigor. Eventually, the hands that were stretched out retract, clutching copper coins, their faces naturally beaming, their hearts full of joy. The unfortunate children still clutching their newspapers gaze blankly at the tram driving away, left with no choice but to wait for future luck.

Inside shops displaying banners advertising huge discounts, Western-style drums are being beaten. The radio broadcasts soothing music, which blends with the sounds of vehicles and horses into the evening symphony of the city.

Matters for Later Discussion 153

— Yue

Shanghai's "Pulling" 154

— Wang Yu

The skill with which Shanghainese "pull" others is truly admirable. If the second landlord's wife, the "good wife" in the side room, and the nanny in the attic decide they want to play mahjong, then the sister-in-law upstairs will invariably be "pulled" to complete the table. However, simply "pulling" is not enough; "pulling" accompanied by witty words is more effective. Thus, the saying "three short of one is bad luck" is uttered, and no "pull" ever fails. Because "pulling" is so wonderful, people who live by "pulling" have emerged.

Every evening, as the lights begin to illuminate, you'll find women with rouge and powder on their faces, acting as enchanting figures weaving through the crowd, their妖形怪狀 and throwing flirtatious glances, grabbing at passersby's sleeves and saying, "Come to my place for fun!" This kind of "pulling" is both firm and gentle, and those who are "pulled" in this way can have their meal expenses for the day taken care of. However, few people pay them any attention, and they can't force their "pulling", making them hateful yet pitiable.

Also, whenever one takes a rickshaw and passes places like Garbage Bridge, small urchins will come up and say, "Sir, let me give you a 'pull'!" and they'll help the rickshaw pull the carriage uphill, hand-in-hand. Once they're done, you have to give them a copper coin. If you refuse, they'll curse you behind your back, calling you "pig," and "old beast", as if it's a kind of "bridge toll" that cannot be avoided.

Recently, due to the economic downturn, the second-hand clothing stores on Shilu Road have also been facing misfortune. Several store owners and employees, anxious and restless, stand inside and outside their counters, clapping bamboo clappers and loudly shouting "Big Discount!" If a passerby glances at the clothes hanging in front of the store, an employee will rush up, grab you, and ask, "What do you need? Sir, we have Indian silk, poplin, everything is here! Don't leave!" This looks as if they are taking you for a big customer, grabbing you and not letting go, so you have to put some effort into twisting your body to get out of their hands. This frightens me so much that I never dare to look again when I pass by next time, to avoid more trouble.

Shanghai's tricks of "pulling" are truly admirable yet fearful!

Little Western Paradise 155

— Written by Zhang Henshui

Chapter 17: Do Not Ask if I'm a Daughter, I'll Never Speak Of My Pain; Compete to See the Face of a Noble Person, All Reverence is Directed Upward

The next day, he got up early and put on his long gown and mandarin jacket, sometimes running inside, sometimes running outside, as if he had lost his soul and had no idea what to do. Because he was always going in and out like this, and he was wearing a mandarin jacket, he attracted the attention of everyone in the hotel. Later, the waiter said that this was Zhang Jiefu, who was putting up slogans. Everyone understood that he was busy preparing for the welcoming event. But apart from seeing him running around, there was no sign of any welcoming ceremony, so no one knew what he was up to. This was the observers' perspective. In fact, Jiefu himself didn't know why he was running around. After twelve o'clock, he was looking to see if the car had arrived. After twelve o'clock, he knew that the car couldn't arrive, so why bother to look? Finally, after two o'clock in the afternoon, there was a commotion in front, and a car drove up. Jiefu hurried to the front to inquire and learned that it was the people sent by the provincial capital to Liuguan to welcome the commissioner, carrying the commissioner's luggage, who had arrived first. It was said that Commissioner Lan and two representatives had gone to Huaqing Pool Hot Springs for a bath and wouldn't arrive for another hour or two. This suited Jiefu's intentions perfectly. He immediately found the messenger escorting the luggage, smiled, and asked, "Excuse me, did Commissioner Lan bring a Secretary Qiu with him?" The messenger said, "No, there is a Secretary Qiu, but he is also in Lintong." Jiefu said, "Ah! It would have been good if he had come first." As he spoke, he accompanied the messenger, pointing out where to place the luggage. The messenger assumed that he was a receptionist sent by the local government, so naturally, he let him handle the reception without objecting. (294)

Fragrant Memories of the Imperial Incense 156

— Original by Princess Der Ling of the Qing Dynasty, translated by Qin Shouou

Third, even though we add lead powder to our type of face powder to keep it from clumping together, just like is done on the outside, we add only a very, very small amount, just enough to keep it from clumping. But face powder made outside the palace walls is often made with lead that's been added without any restraint, so after using it for a year or two, people often deeply suffer from lead poisoning, their faces gradually turning blue, and their skin becoming rough. And some types of face powder even cause a person's face to turn black without them realizing it! If our faces suddenly turned black during court sessions, wouldn't that become a huge joke?!"

The Empress Dowager's sense of humor was sometimes very meaningful. Just imagine, if a solemn and dignified Empress Dowager suddenly appeared with a black face in front of her ministers, wouldn't that be laughably deadly? I imagined this scene, and I almost burst out laughing, but I could only endure it. I dared not laugh, because if I laughed, she would see it in the mirror, and she might force me to explain why it was so funny. How would I answer that?

Although her powder was so elaborate, she used very little of it, unlike ordinary women who would apply a white face that looked like Cao Cao's face. She only applied a very thin layer, which was probably one of her "beauty secrets."

"The rouge we use," she continued, "is even more elaborate to manufacture than the powder. It is made purely from the juice of roses. Rose juice isn't anything rare. It's used a lot in ordinary rouges. But our specialty lies in careful selection." (394)

World News

A Spider with Amazing Strength 157

— Haike

Don't think that a spider is just a small creature in the arthropod class; its strength is far greater than that of a tall, six-foot man. According to zoologists, if its body were as large as a human's, it could easily lift a house with two floors and a roof, like it's nothing. Could a tall, six-foot man do that? So we can say with certainty that a spider's strength is greater than a human's.

In the London Zoo in England, there were two large Ceylonese spiders, the male named "Extreme Meter" and the female named "Sussex." They suddenly disappeared a few years ago, and for twelve months, there was no news of them. Everyone thought they were dead, but a year later, they suddenly returned to the zoo. So some people said that this spider couple probably went somewhere for a honeymoon trip and then rested for a while before returning hand-in-hand. The zoo keepers were naturally very happy. It is said that they lifted a thick piece of glass on the cage when they left. The glass weighed at least two pounds. They both had to use their full strength to lift it up in order to escape. These two spiders were originally from the high mountains of Ceylon. They build huge webs between large trees and rocks, with diameters of up to five feet, and the silk at both ends is ten to twelve feet long, about as thick as lead wire. Birds as large as swallows and larks often get caught in the webs and are eaten by them. Even lizards that people are afraid of have to become their snacks if they get caught in their webs. Their jaws are unusually strong and powerful, like a bird's beak, but they are not poisonous, so humans don't have to be afraid of them.

An English zoologist was walking beside a ditch one day when he saw a large black spider in the ditch, standing there motionless. He found it strange, so he stopped to take a closer look and saw that the spider was catching fish. After a while, it had already bitten onto a fish. Although the fish was not very big, it was more than eight times larger than the spider itself. The spider's fangs were biting the fish's spine tightly, not letting go. The fish struggled desperately, trying to drag the spider into the water, but the spider's hind legs were clinging to the embankment, resisting with force. The fish finally couldn't defeat it and was captured by the spider, which slowly chewed and ate it. Within fifteen minutes, it had achieved complete victory. The spider's great strength can be imagined.

There was also a spider, whose body was only the size of a pea, that built a web on a tall tree. One morning, a mouse half an inch long got caught in the web and couldn't escape. It took the spider a full three hours to wrap its silk around the mouse's tail, tightening it more and more. Finally, it hung the mouse high in the air, which, needless to say, was another full meal for it.

Spiders are not only amazing in their strength but also understand music, and understand the best music. According to reports from the London Zoo, whenever a black spider heard famous music played on the radio, it would crawl out of its hiding place and squat on top of the radio, listening carefully while swaying its body as if keeping time with the music. When the music stopped, it would immediately retreat. The strangest thing is that it only likes the music of the old masters. Sometimes, when it heard jazz music on the radio, it would quickly run away, clearly expressing its disgust. Modern men and women love jazz music in dance halls, and don't seem to appreciate the music of the old masters as much as a small spider does. Hehe!

Free Talk

Two Tendencies of Criticism 177

— Qing Yuan

Professor Croce has a collection of criticisms called "Poetry and Non-Poetry," in which he discusses twenty-six European writers. We have already seen the outlines of his theory in his famous work "Aesthetics." This collection can be said to be a concrete application of his theory. What I find interesting is the essay on Balzac. Because of Balzac's tendency to describe human activities through social environment, he also touched on modern French literary criticism. He said: "I would place the French psychological or impressionistic critics before the didactic and systematizing critics, and place Sainte-Beuve and Lamartine before Taine and Brunetière." Why? "Because these latter are all biased towards theory and are obscured by a kind of intellectual and arbitrary spirit, which constitutes an obstacle to understanding art." He believed that Brunetière did not understand even the most superficial reason, and that the so-called "social novel" was not an art form, but only a dogma. (All the above quotations are from the English translation)

From his argument, we can see two different critical attitudes; Croce and Lamartine, whom he admires, tend to be subjective and impressionistic, starting from the heart and explaining literary phenomena to the outside world. As for Taine and others, they advocate objectivity and positivism, using the external environment to explain its impact on internal activities. Literary criticism can be divided into subjective and objective types according to its own development process, and the degree of development is higher for the latter than the former. No matter how much the former tries to "justify itself," it cannot avoid the metaphysical implications of talking about metaphysics; the latter, in its eagerness to create a system, may sometimes inevitably force facts to fit theory and be subject to arbitrary and mechanical knowledge. However, that kind of positivistic and explanatory spirit can often coincide with the most reasonable modern criticism and converge into a new mainstream, advancing towards a scientific and perfect realm. Because the former is based on an unstable foundation, people can each hold a different view, while the latter can use facts as a touchstone, gradually criticizing, eliminating, reforming, repairing, and approaching the truth that is evident to all.

Croce's theory advocates intuition and advocates breaking the notion of taking the environment of the times as an element of criticism. He believed that art is free and creative and can only be discussed in terms of art itself. However, Taine and others, on the contrary, insisted on seeking explanations from the objective environment of art, and believed that literature is evolutionary and historical and cannot exist in isolation. Therefore, they constantly declared war on the tendency of "art for art's sake." If they were inspired by positivist philosophy, the theory of evolution, and the natural sciences of the time, then Croce precisely expressed a "reaction" to these theories, which has much in common with the vitalism of French and German philosophy; because the starting points are different, the arguments are naturally on separate paths and can never take the same path. However, in my opinion, the abuses of the Taine school are at most that some vulgar literary historians in France regard Taine's theory as the golden rule, unable to measure the advantages and disadvantages of his theory, and unable to further invent his theory, but simply "stiffly" and mechanically" incorporate the incoming literary phenomena into the categories of race, era, and environment, degenerating into arbitrary and superficial. The abuses of Croce and others, on the other hand, will be like the school of Spingarn in the United States, who believe that all expressions are beautiful, vigorously advocate creative criticism, talk emptily and irrelevantly, and only engage in theoretical gossip.

Without mentioning anything else, let's take Croce's writing as an example, in which he said that ancient dramas did not go beyond the limits of studying and portraying ordinary human nature. "But when it came to the seventeenth and eighteenth centuries, the social struggles and changes and the rising historical interest, on the one hand, echoed on the comedy, making it express a certain social and historical environment, and on the other hand, occupied the novel, turning it into a 'historical' and 'social' novel." He said that Balzac "does not hope to limit himself to simple observation, but to discover the reasons and laws of social phenomena, and further to trace and evaluate the principles of goodness, truth, and beauty." But what are these changes for? What is the "cause" of these things? Croce only described these phenomena without revealing the latent causes and meanings, which would not satisfy people. To be honest, in order to give a clear explanation of these phenomena, it seems that objective investigation is needed, and to "keep your feet on the ground" to work on the study of the external environment!

Literary critic Lanson said in his famous History of French Literature that Taine and Brunetière opened a new page in the history of criticism. The great development of modern natural science has also provided many methods to make literary criticism tend to be solid and certain. For past critics, praise and scolding are superfluous. Brunetière's argument is now dilapidated, and even Taine, who is called the most able to maintain an "objective attitude," has finally fallen into the quagmire of idealism in his application of methods? History is evolving, and some people have followed them to open a new page in the history of criticism. Only their down-to-earth interpretation of the influence of works on each other and their relationship with the changes in the objective environment has been unprecedented and can be regarded as the forerunner of modern criticism.

A Dirge of Life 178

— Ye Cao

One evening, I was strolling along the wall of the village.

Suddenly, carried by the wind, came a kind of dismal cry from somewhere. The sound was long and low, as if something was covering the caller's throat, and yet he was still shouting in his struggle.

Terrifying, dreadful, the sound started again. Just like the first time, like the dying moan of a victim, desolate, heartbroken; I was so stirred that my eyes widened, my entire nervous system was enveloped, as if attracted by some force, I tried my best to find the origin of the sound.

I stopped outside the attached building wall of a landlord's house. I thought, here might be some new discovery. This is an indispensable building for landlords, located in the back row of the entire residence, not large in structure, but with quite a few rooms, usually used as a warehouse.

I leaned against a tree, looking in through the small window of the attached building. A gloomy lamp hung in the middle of the wall, opposite it was a terrible young farmer, he was hanging from the beam, his face pale, the whites of his eyes facing the ground:

"Tell me! Tell me! Hurry up and tell me!"

As he spoke, he received several lashes on the young farmer's shoulders! The young farmer only glanced at him, not saying a word. The person holding the whip was our small village chief, a big guy with a face full of brutality: confirming that he was rich and powerful.

"Speak! I want you to say it yourself!"

Again, several lashes, the young farmer remained silent, quiet, he didn't even sigh. This aroused the small village chief's anger even more, he brandished the leather whip and lashed again, that ferocious face looked just like a beast!

"What do you want him to say? You..."

A woman knelt beside the small village chief, she wept, her voice trembling. She was the young farmer's wife, working as a hired woman in the small village chief's house. Originally, they rented the village chief's land, but due to the poor harvest that year, all the farming was undertaken by her husband.

"I mean..." the small village chief was a little embarrassed; women after all have magic, his tone immediately changed: "I mean, when can you pay back the grain you owe me?" The small village chief wanted to use these words to deceive the woman out, he felt unusually uneasy about the woman's sudden arrival, naturally, this was extremely inconvenient for the progress of his business.

"Big Master," the woman pleaded, "didn't I tell you, as soon as the wheat season comes next year, we will definitely pay it off! We don't eat much!"

"Go away, I will release him immediately—" the small village chief said to the woman with the tenderness he used to have for her, smiling, moving his eyes to the corner of his eye.

"Okay."

The woman watched with her own eyes as the small village chief released her husband, then slowly walked away. Her husband, powerless, slumped on the ground, his eyes tightly closed, his breathing very uneven.

The small village chief revealed a victorious expression, that posture was like a triumphant knight. He lit a cigarette, pacing back and forth in the dim light. Suddenly, he changed color, kicking the young farmer hard in the back:

"Tell me! Tell me! What did you say to people!"

"..." The young man did not answer.

"You speak! You ruined my reputation! I fuck your mother! You harmed me, I... tell me!"

"..."

"Speak, you poor wretch! What about me and your wife?"

"..."

The leather whip was waving again! Just as his second whip was about to fall, the young farmer somehow broke the rope and jumped up. He rushed over quickly, pointing his finger tightly at the small village chief's neck.

Hardly a sound could be heard, they were somersaulting and rolling on the ground, two pairs of eyes full of anger, hostile, with fire in them! That fire separated by a vast gulf! The dim light painted silhouettes of the struggle between these two pairs of fire on the wall.

"Ah..."

With such a cry, the small village chief fell down! I saw his blood flowing, his last throbbing; a terrifying atmosphere surrounded me, I fell from the tree to the ground again, I passed out!

The next day, people told me that the small village chief was stabbed to death by his maid, and the maid fled with her injured husband!

Tragedy on the Seashore (7) 179

— Original by French Balzac, Translated by Wang Jiansheng

"What you said to your mother will make the problem even more serious. Let's talk about the main issue. "Do you still want to get a pardon?" "Yes." "Wait a minute," he said, "was there a cross marked on the gold coin too? The cross on the coin was marked by a sardine merchant when he gave us the money." Jia Aokuis finally understood, he cried, "We have said a lot," Pi said; "I will not mention anything about your past, but I don't want a Chaiboleimei family member to die in the Kelo Yixike market. Pray, we have to hurry up and paste it. Within a minute, a monk will come to hear your confession." His mother had already walked away, she could not bear to stay there and hear her son being convicted.

When she had already walked away, his uncle Chai Boleimei led a pastor from Piliaok to come; but Aokuis didn't have anything to say to him, he was a cunning person, he knew that his father's unwillingness to confess would not lead him to death. Chai Boleimei saw that Jia Aokuis was very stubborn, so he said, "Sir, thank you, please forgive me, but I want to give my son a big lesson, I ask you not to say anything more about this matter, as for you," he said to Jia Aokuis, "if you are not angry, this matter cannot be changed, I will solve this matter without hesitation. He sent him to bed. The child believed this, but he guessed that he could get his father's forgiveness, he slept, his father watched over him. When he saw his son falling asleep, he covered his mouth with linen, and tightly bound it with a canvas, finally tightening his hands and feet. He went crazy, he wept blood," as Chai Boleimei told the magistrate. You can imagine his mother kneeling in front of his father to beg for forgiveness. "He has been sentenced!" he said, "You have to help me put him in the boat," she refused this request, Chai Boleimei put him in the boat himself, forced him to the bottom of the boat, and tied a stone around his neck. Then he rowed out of the small bay—all the way out to the sea, to the rock where he is now sitting. At that time, the poor mother had asked her husband's brother to take her there, she shouted at the top of her voice: "Mercy!" But to no avail. It was a moonlit night, she saw her husband throw their son into the sea. The sea was calm, she only heard the sound of splashing water, and then nothing, no trace, no bubbles. No, the sea does not reveal any secrets, Chai Boleimei landed and comforted his wife's moans, but she was half dead, it was impossible for one brother to take her with him, they had no choice but to put her in the small boat that had just carried his son, rowing deep along the waterways of Kelo Yixike. Ah! This beautiful Boli tribe person left this world in less than a week. At the time of her death, she also asked her husband to burn that cursed small boat. He did as she asked. For the sake of his son, he had finished everything, he didn't know what else he needed. When he walked, he seemed unsteady on his feet like someone who was drunk, so he traveled for ten days, and when he came back, he sat where you saw him. He hasn't said a word since he sat there.

An Unconventional Group (Part 2) 180

— Zhou Wen

"I wrote another poem yesterday, this..." he said.

"Oh?" The pale face's mouth corner held a smile, then he turned his face over again, half-opening his lips. Seeing the master's lips trembling, he thought he was about to recite, his head lowered towards the master's lips, unconsciously swaying on his neck with relish.

"No, no,... don't recite it." The master suddenly said to himself again. "Actually, after reading your poem 'Let's Touch This Cup!', mine should be burned..."

"Where, where." The pale face said repeatedly; so moved that his steps were a little unsteady. He looked at the master, then very sincerely stretched out a slender finger and gently patted the master's shoulder twice. "You are too modest, you are too humble! Actually, I have said long ago, among these poets, only you are the most promising. I, actually, am about to be what is called 'yesterday's flower'," he finished speaking, he was immediately very satisfied with the rhetoric of his words, neither raising others too high, nor demeaning himself too much, very in line with the doctrine of the mean. A smile appeared on the corner of his mouth.

But the master was also moved, his face shining with oil, his cheekbones almost as red as his lips, the light in his eyes simply flashing. But he calmed down, immediately glancing at the pale face and saying:

"That is indeed your humility. The friends of our Lotus Poetry Society often say, now in China, who else is there besides you?"

The pale face now seemed to have drunk a large bowl of wine, completely intoxicated, his eyes simply burning, his unsteady feet, stepping on the terrazzo floor simply as if stepping on a velvet carpet. Stepping into a door frame, facing the dressing mirror standing against the wall twenty feet away, the white light of Kiyonga Ikkou shone brightly, clearly illuminating the shadow of himself walking ahead of the master with oily hair; the pale face's cheeks were red, his forehead flashing with oil, his long, slender frame wearing a light blue patterned silk shirt, his shoulders sloping, the hem of the blue silk shirt simply lightly fluttering in front of his legs. He deeply stared at this shadow that he felt was very suave, even he himself felt very lovable. But the mirror flashed and fell behind him, but he always felt attracted by it, as if it wanted to pull his head over; but he endured, endured; but finally turned his head back, but could only see the side of the upright mirror frame. It wasn't until the master stretched out his hand to him, and pointed to a long fat face and a round fat face in front of him, that he was surprised to take a closer look, and realized that he was in the living room.

"This is Boss Wang. This is Boss Liu." The master said.

The long fat face and the round fat face immediately clenched their fists and cupped their hands repeatedly.

"Hehe, I've heard of you for a long time!" The long fat face said.

"Hehe, I've heard of you for a long time! Actually, we met at Mr. Huang's place that time." The round fat face said.

The pale face was surprised, his palms moved at the sides of his legs, "Should I raise them up?" He quickly thought this, but finally raised them up, awkwardly clenching his fists and cupping his hands.

"Hehe," he said, the roots of his ears suddenly turning red, red to his cheeks.

The master glanced at the pale face, immediately remembering what the pale face had just said.

"Ah, damn! How did I bring him in front of businessmen..." So he immediately stretched out his hands towards the pale face's chest, making a gesture as if to hug him and said:

"Ah, Mr. Huang and the others have a few poems here, how about you critique them for them, ah? Let's go over there?"

"Hehe," the pale face said with a smile, the moment he turned his face to the master, his eyes paused on the round fat face for a second, to see if he was flashing admiring eyes or opening his mouth in surprise.

The round fat face also stretched out his hands, his ten fat fingers straightened, his body flashed and he paced two steps away, his hand also embraced the empty chair and laughed:

"Ah, please sit on this one. Sit down. We are not strangers. Don't be polite."

"Ah, ah," the pale face nodded and said. "Don't be polite, don't be polite."

The master asked the pale face to walk towards the dressing mirror, when the two of them passed side by side through the middle of the room, next to the round table with a vase and a white cloth, the voices of the two fat faces rang behind them:

"Ah, ah, really, don't say it anymore, this year's business! That batch of goods I just mentioned, yesterday it was three taels and two, today it suddenly fell to three taels..."

A Group on a Summer Night 181

— Long Zaitian

The setting sun swept a dazzling halo across the lawn of the vast forest, the shadows of the poplars were also lengthened on the ground; the privet and juniper trees on both sides of the sidewalk, in an orderly manner, interweaved four thick lines; the shadows of clumps of Scotch pine climbed like squirrels; the willow leaves were swaying messily, as if something was stirring under this huge flowered carpet,... the slightly red lotus buds just emerging from the water, in the shade of the mountain, were panting娇喘among countless green lotus leaves. The street lamps hidden in the shade of the maple and French parasol trees on both sides of the road also began to flicker with yellow light.

At this time, Kang Yu, Li Mi, and Ke Liangfu had, as usual, eaten dinner, and, as usual, instructed the tea servant to move the rattan chairs and tea table to the革坪, and also brewed a pot of white tea and a pot of green tea, to welcome the curtain of night, thrown down from the写窿 upper sky.

"Little Kang, have you eaten?" was a greeting with a Zhejiang accent from someone with the surname Shi; sometimes a middle-aged man with a big belly would come along, but not always. After sitting down, they would, as usual, talk about the objects that Ke Liangfu had not yet understood, in a burst of satisfied laughter, everyone would 打着九尾龟上学来的够作呕的苏白: 窝心得来!"

Then: Little Li would straighten his voice and hum a 犂 or Beijing opera tune.

In this way, the quiet dusk became lively. Only Ke Liangfu was呆呆的, because he was truly an outsider to the big drum. In this way, he raised his head alone, silently observing the surroundings of nature.

The crescent moon was already hanging in the mountain depression; her satellites also sparkled and followed her appearance; the fiery sunset had changed into dense clouds of green-gray; the mountains near and far were all dressed in evening clothes; fireflies glittered like shooting stars; the handle of the Great Dipper, the only thing he recognized, was also clearly outlined one by one. The green蛀 in the lotus pond, responding to the applause here, were constantly "阁哇, 阁哇"鼓噪...

Little Li's voice became louder and louder, and he began to sing the scolding of 流水板. However, Ke Liangfu still could not understand Beijing opera at all. And Tong and Kang seemed to have also shifted their interests, and were talking in low voices about their Mei Fen and Mei Ying, which forced Ke Liangfu to continue to quietly look at the sky.

The Milky Way's light band had clearly traversed the sky, Taurus was sparkling above his head, the hot velvet curtain was scattered like a fishing net. The treetops were dotted with rice-drawn black dots, the lines of the distant mountains were also blurred, the dots of electric fire in the distance were also shining through, and our group changed the topic again, and were laughing and talking in a tumultuous manner.
