Further Discussion on the Responsibility of Children's Marriage 182

— Fei

The other day, Xu Zhihui, the accountant of a wild game shop in Caishi Street, committed suicide due to being unable to repay his debts for his children's marriage. The reporter's thoughts led to the article "The Responsibility of Children's Marriage". As the idea was not exhausted, here are some more supplements.

In the future, the responsibility for children's marriage problems should naturally fall on the children themselves, as mentioned in the previous article. However, now is still a transitional era. Most children receive considerable education in schools or learn considerable professions in society. They have more time to contact the opposite sex, and free marriage is relatively easy. If daughters are bound by the old family ethics, some hire teachers to study at home, and some drop out of school for fear that their daughters will engage in indecent behavior outside. Even if they are studying at school, because the concept of old ethics is deeply imprinted in their minds, they still have the idea of "how can I see my mother with shame". Such daughters originally do not have the ability to be free, and only their fathers and brothers can introduce or make decisions. Only the current transitional era has such women. In the future, they will definitely be gradually assimilated.

Secondly, there are many abuses of free marriage. In the past, divorce cases were uncommon in autocratic marriages. Now, with free marriage, divorce cases are springing up like mushrooms after rain. It is an inevitable principle that easy marriage also leads to easy divorce. For fathers and brothers in charge, they usually have considerable guidance, and have the responsibility to agree or disagree at the time, but in fact, once a man and woman have reached the point of passionate love, the agreement or disagreement of their fathers and brothers is completely equal to a blank document.

Some say that since men and women have a high level of knowledge, they will naturally have considerable ability to make decisions and will not be fooled by others. This is not entirely true. For example, the other day the newspaper reported from Belgrade that Mania had eighty wives in five years. I think foreign women must have a higher level of knowledge than Chinese women, and among these eighty girls, there must be several who are very knowledgeable, that can be stated, however, they cannot avoid being deceived. This situation is evident, on the contrary, there may be women like Mania, so how can men not be deceived by them? Such drawbacks are inevitable in the belief in free marriage.

The above issues seem to be discussed too far, and have nothing to do with the responsibility of children's marriage, but they are extremely relevant. Because parents are not responsible for their children's marriage problems, then for all the unfortunate consequences that occur after marriage, parents also do not have to bear the responsibility. Then, children must also pay more attention to the issue of marriage themselves.

In short, now that social interactions have been made public and women have been liberated, there is originally no problem between men and women, but now people still regard the issue of social ethics as an extremely important problem in society, it is no different than fighting against the tide of the times.

Autumn Rain Serenade 183

— Liang Qijun

The small boat glides gently on the river surface with a smiling crinkled face.

Outside the cabin—rain is falling softly.

It's autumn.

This should be said to be autumn rain.

After spending the season of autumn rain, everything will return to the silence of winter.

People, hiding in that narrow, cramped cabin, are in a depressed mood. In their hearts, they unconsciously feel a touch of dim melancholy. Like the misty autumn rain, giving the nearby forests, the continuous hills, and the ancient city walls, a layer of hazy gray.

From what time did I understand the loveliness of melancholy, I can't remember clearly. However, as soon as autumn arrives, that suffocating depression pressed on my heart comes along with the autumn wind. On the one hand, I feel it is lovely, on the other hand, I feel a kind of disappointment and resentment.

"In summer, I had dreams every night. Now that summer is over, those dreams have disappeared with the last roses of summer.

"Friend, you should know, how I regret the passing of my youth.

"Today, it is even more gloomy.

"—Why are you so depressed?

"I can't answer your question; don't you understand me?

"So, thinking of myself, tonight, I will be sleepless because of this."

Thinking of the words written in my friend's notebook, I can only stare blankly, with a melancholy wry smile. There is a special feeling between us; so I scooped out the passion hidden deep in my heart.

But, who can understand themselves better than themselves!

In the summer, I felt hatred, annoyance, resentment, and all kinds of displeasure everywhere. I thought that when autumn came, the weather would be cool, and the heart crouched in depression could spend some happy days in the high and clear autumn.

But, after all, I was disappointed.

I will never find it strange that disappointment closely follows the advent of hope. Expectation and bubbles are, in my eyes, as ordinary as flowers blooming and falling. Since I became sensible, a long string of days has passed in that disappointed mood, deceiving myself with hope, spending spring, and then spending autumn.

Sometimes, in the quiet of the night, gazing at the clean and beautiful sky like dark blue velvet, the moon walks through the clouds. In my heart, I will think: if I really keep walking like this, when will it end? —This is a question that cannot be answered.

The desolation of dusk, the haziness of autumn rain, the sky is getting darker.

Tonight, it is a sky where you can't see the moon again. —I thought. My heart felt like a cold wind had blown?…

Outside the cabin—rain is falling softly.

It's autumn.

Flight (Part 2) 184

— Jin Guang

A gust of evening wind thickened the desolation of autumn, the frightening sound of falling leaves, stirring everyone's shivering hearts; the children were all nestled tightly in their mothers' arms, trembling silently; the elderly's weak bodies were also leaning on the shoulders of the strong, only waves of sick moans, piercing the hearts of their companions. A few days of traveling at night had trained them to be very calm, there was no noise, no crying in fear, and even less resentment, only people close to people, hearts connected to hearts, silently and solemnly, in the terrifying night forest, making a flight without a home.

Although the road was unfamiliar, it still extended endlessly under their feet. —People are like a flock of crows without a home.

It was a pitch-black团; no moonlight, no firelight, not a single light; people were walking in the dark hell, except for being able to see half of their own body, they couldn't see anything else, except for being able to hear their own hurried breathing, they could only hear the breathing of others, many people couldn't hold on. In their hearts, they all called out 'Stop! Stop, it's the same as not being able to live!' But they were unwilling to say it out loud; after all, they thought that behind them were the swallowing flood, and the terrible claws of the demons in the dark, so they struggled again and followed the crowd, their numb legs didn't seem to feel anything anymore.

It wasn't until the dusk of the second day that they rushed to an ancient town; quiet, desolate, telling them that they were also a group of people caught in hunger, cold, and desolation.

Sparse smoke from the cooking fires, stirring a string of hungry eyes, they couldn't help but shake their empty bellies, swallowing a mouthful of dust-covered saliva.

But the people in that village had long known their origins from their clothing covered in dust; they had detected their situation from the faces with shadows; without waiting for them to speak, they said to them:

'The year is not good, we don't have the ability to keep you in town.'

A sigh, the dusk became even more bleak; step by step, they still rushed into the lurking darkness; they passed another foreign land!

Mountain after mountain, river after river, one village after another, passed under their tired feet; they made a flight without a home. —They were a group of homeless refugees.

Haziness 185

— Chen Liang

I didn't look at the clock when I stumbled out of the room. Judging from the chatter of the sparrows on the yellow leaves, it felt quite early. The milky white sky was inlaid with a few patches of pale gray clouds. The weather was cool. A gust of wind brought a shower of rain, and the rain stopped when the wind passed. I donned my black rain cape, put the cigarette holder in my mouth, and was led by a yellow dragonfly with black spots, through the bamboo forest, and then through the small path inlaid with tile shards in patterns between the rows of willow trees. Thin moss grew sparsely on the path. Although very subtle, it was full of vitality, unlike the bamboo leaves, maple leaves, and willow branches, which couldn't withstand the pressure of the rain and the blowing of the wind, and drooped low, displaying a tired posture.

My usual spot for sitting is always by the lake, idly gazing at the blue waves and green mountains...

However, today's scenery is different again. After the rain, the green mountains are gone, the blue waves are gone, and the brown sails drifting in the distance are gone. From the clumps of reeds growing on the lake surface, there is only a vast expanse of hazy territory. If a tourist who has never been here before, he would definitely think that there is a vast and promising future in the haze, or that there is a verdant plain over there, and would never expect that high mountains, steep cliffs, strange rocks, deep caves, and thorns full of sharp spines are hidden in the misty haze ahead. The boatmen do not like this hazy lake surface. They are afraid of steering the boat in the wrong direction and accidentally hitting the reefs hidden in the water, the remnants of the mountains. I watched the few masts carefully approaching the lake beach and flowing past, without any sound. The lake water was calm and gleaming with white light, like solidified jelly, fully revealing the loneliness of life.

I sat on a damp stone and gently blew out a puff of smoke. From the smoke rings that suddenly grew larger and then burst, a dark tide of thought quietly arose:

"My own life is often obscured by haziness, preventing me from recognizing the truth, the world, and sin. I cannot reflect the meaning of existence and the center of thought, and yet I timidly hold a weak heart, walking step by step on the edge of the journey of life. I am afraid of accidentally entering the pit of sin, afraid of touching the insidious reefs, and also afraid of going in the wrong direction on the road of life. 'Caution' is often ridiculed as 'cowardice,' but occasionally being a little bolder will be condemned by that kind of 'morality,' and then the present becomes even more hazy. Should I simply close my eyes and live in confusion, letting precious time flow by like water in confusion?"...

I remember living in the city, morning, evening, or rainy days, walking onto the rooftop terrace and looking around, the red rooftops, gray high-rise buildings, black iron chimneys, and red lighthouses, the crisscrossing electric wires... vaguely hidden in the smoke and turned into a hazy scene; intense appetites, sinister conspiracies, licentiousness, madness, sin: everything was obscured, so it was often easy to think of a fairyland and feel the breadth and joy of the realm of life. However, this is still a smokescreen, and behind the smokescreen are heavy bombs! Therefore, I cannot look at the haze with satisfaction, like a poet or painter.

The guy who was on duty watching the night in the garden passed by with heavy steps. A spark of a just discarded cigarette butt was extinguished. A black ant crawled over the flattened cigarette butt. I was happy for this ant, but the weather was still so gloomy, and the lake surface was still so hazy. I couldn't help but feel a dark sorrow for the situation before me. The blue waves and green mountains I longed for?…

Zhou Jianhong's Big Red Robe

Oriental (1020) 11:00 AM to 12:00 PM

Opening "Newly Compiled Blessed Man"

Suzhou is a place of blessed people.

Go to find a blessed person in the team.

Still a class of concubines.

Shamelessly possessing millions in assets.

Living in luxury and being extraordinarily refined.

Enjoying the peaceful blessings of Jiangnan.

How would they know about the disasters of the people in the north?

The newly built foreign-style house is truly exquisite.

Willow shade, winding path, and deep sounds from the pavilion.

The courtyard has a terrazzo floor.

The door is made of spruce.

Hundreds of electric lights shine brightly.

Mandarin ducks sing by the lotus pond.

The lawn is evenly green and covers the ground.

The winding path leads to a secluded spot with lush flowers and trees.

Young people have many pleasant pastimes.

The young couple goes to the cool pavilion to escape the summer heat.

The interior is elaborately furnished.

The calligraphy and paintings are signed by famous people.

At night, there are fragrant flowers and the moon is shady.

The big and small rooms are mostly modernized.

The teak furniture is exquisite.

Five-colored carpets are laid neatly.

Western-style sunshades on all sides.

Electric fans never stop day and night.

Living and eating are all luxurious.

Iced Dutch water.

Banana ice cream.

Sizzling stir-fry with new flavors.

The husband is favored and his heart is joyful.

It is difficult to sell a beauty's heart with gold.

Spend all the gold without being stingy.

Cultivated in the previous life to receive in this life.

How many lifetimes can the plum blossom cultivate?

Worthy to be called a satisfactory person in the world.

Chen Ruilin Chen Yunlin Golden Fan

Oriental (1020) 1:00 PM to 2:00 PM

Opening "Lament in Sickness"

Qiu Xia's poems from that year said.

Autumn rain and autumn wind kill people with sorrow.

Sudden rain and sunshine change the weather.

Carelessly one will get sick.

In the summer, one is still healthy.

Several times of autumn wind and autumn rain.

A healthy person turns into a sick person.

Headaches, fever, and chills.

The whole body is weak and the heart is uneasy.

Taking medicine and seeing a doctor for a week.

(Fortunately) The expert of internal medicine, Zhu Qi, could make the body light.

Relatives and friends come to comfort.

That is all of you listeners.

The cause of the illness in the call.

I am always grateful for this matter.

Thank you all for your love and care.

Health is happiness in life.

Heroes fear illness the most.

The words of the ancients are not deceiving.

Xing Ruiting's Opening

Mingyuan (960) 1:00 PM to 2:00 PM

Opening "Advising Not to Eat Opium"

Lying lazily on the couch and enjoying oneself.

Why ever leave the house in all seasons?

The light of a lamp is hard to compare to a bean.

But it is more enchanting than electric light.

Three or five friends lying together.

Nothing more than spitting out mist and swallowing clouds.

A handgun is not as good as an opium pipe.

Happiness is found only in opium.

Precious money is used wrongly.

Giving up one's rights to others.

I advise you all to listen carefully.

Only opium addiction harms one's entire life.

It can make a father and son become enemies.

It can make a husband and wife lack affection.

It can make brothers no longer righteous.

It can make relatives and friends look down on you.

It can make it impossible to protect a thousand-year foundation.

It can make one's family and business decline and be invaded by others.

All day long, the red sun rises and one goes into a dream.

One is energetic in the middle of the night.

Turning day and night upside down.

Spending time unknowingly.

A seven-foot man should have ambition.

How can one seek pleasure and neglect youth?

Time is like water and cannot be regained.

One must be famous.

I hope my compatriots quickly quit opium.

Everyone will be energetic.

Please forgive me, Ruiting, for not being bold.

But daring to write a worldly admonition.

You must forgive me for my sincerity.

Interesting Anecdotes on the Location Shoot of "Triumphant Song" 194

Yuan Meiyun was so frightened that she yelled "pig"! Guan Pangzi sang "Wang Baochuan" loudly.

Bu Wancang directed the sound film "Triumphant Song." The crew set off for Hangzhou Zhuji the day before yesterday for location shooting. Yesterday, we received a letter from Chen Linshu, the stage director, reporting the situation along the way, which was quite humorous. I have recorded it to make you laugh.

Our "Triumphant Song" location crew took the 9:30 AM express train from Shanghai Fanxue Ferry. Arriving in Hangzhou at 3:30 PM, they chartered five cars and drove to the Jiangbian in Nanxing Bridge, and then chartered a small steamer directly to Zhuji. They arrived at the residence of Mr. Pan, a friend of Mr. Bu, at 11:30 PM. The working location is there. Here is a small report on the journey.

The day of departure was the day when Nie Er's memorial service was held in Shanghai Jincheng. We were unable to attend because of work, which was of course very unsettling. However, on the ship, Yuan Meiyun, Wang Yin, Jiang Xiu, Liu Li, Jin Yi, Ge Aina, etc., in order to express their condolences to the spirit of this progressive composer, sang "Escape Song" composed by Nie Er. At this time, they passed the small town of Linpu and suddenly saw electric lights everywhere. We were very surprised and asked the boatman, who told us that the Ullambana Festival was being held to super-transcend the souls.

At that time, Mr. Bu spoke, asking everyone to be quiet for one minute to express condolences. Afterwards, because the tide was high and almost level with the bridge, the boat could not pass, so it was parked on the shore. Everyone stretched their necks and looked into the distance, seeing only black shadows, and the rustling of grass and trees made people shiver. At this point, Yuan Meiyun was the first to flee into the cabin, and the rest followed suit. Then, the sound of "wow woo" came from the shore. Amnia said that the red man was coming, frightening Yuan Meiyun to yell "pig!"

Inside the cabin, bored, Qin Tong imitated Yuan Meiyun's singing of "Picking Lotus Song" in "Triumphant Song." Zhang Yide sang a Hua Dan role, making people's muscles twitch. Qin Tong had a very good appetite, unconsciously so. Guan Hongda and Zhao Tushan sang "Joining the Army," Guan played Wang Baochuan, and Zhao played Xue Pinggui. The singing was done with acting, which was much more humorous than listening to "Freedom Dance." Everyone burst out laughing. Then, Wu Weiyun and Gu Zongyi sang "Ma Lang Dang" and "Little Widow" in a completely Suzhou accent, making people laugh to tears.

Today (17th), Bu and Wu are looking for location scenes in the morning, filming in the afternoon, and there are many planes at night. The mosquito nets are ineffective, and it is impossible to sleep well. It is probably because Hangzhou has an aviation school.

This departure has a crew of 58 people, lasting about a month. It is possible to return soon. There are more than 100 pieces of luggage and ten water pumps, belts, etc., and the entire set of costumes for "Fishing Family," the scene is grand to the extreme.

The goods in my belly are almost gone, I will report again tomorrow.

Shenbao Architectural Weekly

Japanese Temple Architecture (4) 195

— Ito Chuta (Author) Zhang Guangzheng (Translator)

The Architecture of Tsukiji Hongwanji Temple

Related to the above, I would like to talk about the recently renovated Tsukiji Hongwanji Temple. This building was actually designed by me under the commission of the temple, and I am now explaining it here again, which is a bit inappropriate. I ask for your indulgence. At first, I made two designs according to the wishes of the temple, one purely Japanese style and one Indian style. After careful deliberation by the temple authorities, the Indian style was selected. Based on the reasons mentioned above and the requirements of the Oka plan, I also felt that the Indian style was better. Here, I am doing my best to achieve it. Because this is a new attempt with no precedent, it is of course expected to become a major issue in the architectural world. Sure enough, voices of praise and criticism rose from all sides, for which I am grateful. However, there are many misunderstandings among them, and I feel it is necessary to explain them.

Some people say that the building is a modern and gorgeous building; others criticize it as being quite similar to the Nicholas Church; others feel that there is no such style in the Saracenio and Indian styles; and a certain magazine mocks the designer for not knowing the difference between the Saracenio and Indian styles. Here, I will not go into detail one by one, but only think of a simple word. First, is the relationship with Nicholas Church: The architecture of Nicholas Church is called "Russian Eastern Romanesque." The Eastern Romanesque style contains a strong oriental color. This oriental color is mainly Persian, and it can be traced back to India even further. That is to say, the style of Nicholas Church naturally has an Indian style flavor hidden in its bones. Therefore, it is not bad eyesight to see the two as resembling each other.

Secondly, it is not without reason to mistake the Hongwanji Temple as a Saracenio building. Originally, the Saracenio building originated in the Arab region. Later, it was greatly influenced by the prosperity of Islam and Eastern architecture such as Eastern Rome and Persia before it reached its peak. However, Mr. Hauer, an authority on the study of Indian art history, said that Saracenio architecture was greatly influenced by Indian architecture. In short, there is a connection between Saracenio architecture and ancient Indian architecture. Therefore, modern Saracenio architecture and Indian architecture are often confused and difficult to distinguish. The architecture of Hongwanji Temple is based on the ancient Indian style, but if you carefully examine its many modern handcrafts, it is easy to mistake it for a Saracenio style, which is a fact.

Secondly, fundamentally speaking, there are many people who criticize that the Hongwanji Temple's choice of Indian style was a bad choice, which is due to different opinions. As mentioned earlier, tracing back to the roots of Buddhism and basing it on the Indian style is theoretically, materially, structurally, and in terms of the luxurious nature, the relationship of labor costs, all of which are very appropriate. However, I am not saying that it is appropriate for all sects and various Buddhist buildings across Japan to adopt the Indian style. (End)

From Architectural Art to the Temples of Greece (VII) 196

— Sun Zongwen

——The Most Glorious Page in the History of World Architecture——

(IV) Sculpture and Color of Greek Temples

The fame of Greek architectural art in the world is also due to the beauty of the sculptures on its buildings. Originally, Greek sculpture art was also a glorious and splendid page in the history of world art, occupying an extremely important position. When the Greeks designed a building, the architect and the sculptor cooperated with each other, so the products presented a spirit of harmony, and no inferior works appeared. In addition, most of the building materials were made of extremely beautiful and pleasing stone blocks, such as marble, and the Greek sculptors used their skilled techniques to create them carefully; no wonder their temples were worshipped by the world!

On Greek temples, the most important places for sculpture are the Pediment, Metope, and Freize; the stories of the sculptures mostly tell the life stories of the gods enshrined in the temple, or the battles between the race and the gods; the most common and most sculpted story is the battle between the half-man, half-horse animal Centaurus and the Lapitha tribe. Other things varied depending on the time and place, but the sculpting techniques were always very sophisticated. At that time, the most famous Greek sculptors were Phidias and Scopas. The styles of the two were unique, and the latter's works were the most fashionable and representative of the national character at the time. The former's representative work is the Parthenon Temple, and the latter's representative work is the Ionic Temple; the former temple is a famous building in the history of world architecture, while the latter is one of the seven wonders of the world. The greatness of the two buildings is enough to represent the superb skills of these two sculptors. It is also sufficient to represent the highest point of Greek art at that time. The appearance of these two sculptors added a layer of magic to the magnificent temples at the time.

Whether a building is harmonious or not is closely related to the beauty of the building. The so-called "harmony" has two aspects: first, the harmony of form, and second, the harmony of color. The former has been mentioned earlier, and the latter is what we are going to talk about now.

Greek temples also paid great attention to the harmony of colors; because they often carved landscapes and figures on fleshy marble such as Penteric and Parian marble, and because the colors of the materials were beautiful and elegant, their works also presented a spirit of harmony. Also, we know that people without cultural education always like to apply deep, eye-catching, and extremely strong colors to buildings, such as red, blue, etc. Many temples in ancient times were in this situation; however, although Greek temples were influenced by legacy and customs, they did make a lot of progress in terms of color. They mostly painted the important parts of the color, such as the deep parts that cannot be seen from a distance, with light colors on them; in this way, the inherent sculptural beauty would not be destroyed. In short, they wrote with "beauty" as the only condition. Because of the beauty of their colors and the rarity of their materials, no wonder their temples were so amazing!

Based on the above conclusions, we can know that Greek temples are indeed great, delicate, and rare, and they are indeed the most brilliant page in the history of world architectural art! The greatness of its architectural art in terms of skills is enough to give people a different impression; it is an unforgettable page of historical relics for everyone engaged in the architectural business, in our minds. However, the most regrettable thing is that due to the long years and the changes in historical events, the most famous temples in history have now been destroyed and no longer exist! Even if there are any, they are only fragments of sculptures from the temples that are still preserved in the British Museum, just for people to commemorate and pay their respects! However, isn't everything in the world like this?! (The End)

Materials Science of Architecture (Continued) (Previous) 197

— Zhu Zhenmu

Chapter 8 Zinc

Section 1 Overview of Zinc

Because zinc is very active when it is in a metallic state, there are no individual mineral seedlings. It is usually chemically transformed into zinc sulfide and buried. Therefore, all zinc mines are sulfides.

Section 2 Smelting of Zinc

The smelting of zinc is also divided into two methods: retort method and electrolytic method.

(1) Retort Method—Use a retort made of white porcelain sand. Place coal powder and fine zinc ore powder inside the retort. The usual proportion is 40% to 75% of coal powder, and the coal powder is best made of white coal and other anthracite. After mixing, heat it together outside the retort. Heating and burning coal, coal gas or other fuels are all acceptable. Connected to the retort is a ceramic air cooler and a cast iron condensing box. When zinc is distilled and gasified from the retort, it can be condensed into a liquid through this box, and it can be taken out from the bottom of the box.

(2) Electrolytic Method! First, roast the mineral seedlings, refine them once, and add sulfuric acid to release some of the liquid, which is converted into sulfur dioxide and dissipated, and the zinc electrons are reduced from the zinc sulfate and attached to the iron plate. Moreover, if sulfur and iron ore are mixed, magnets can be used to separate this substance into two parts. The part containing vaporized zinc can be put into sulfuric acid for further treatment to obtain a zinc sulfate solution. This acidic solution is then mixed with the part that does not contain vaporized zinc to neutralize it. Through this neutralizing chemical change, the iron is converted into iron hydroxide and automatically precipitates. At the same time, impurities such as arsenic, silicon, and antimony sand can also sink together. Then, the pure zinc is completely attached to the electrode plate, and it can be taken out.

Section 3 Properties and Applications of Zinc

Zinc is grayish-white, is not susceptible to erosion by air and moisture, is very conductive, and is ductile, but its resistance is not strong. The maximum resistance of cast zinc is only 9,000 pounds per square inch, and if it is rolled and cut, it is only 24,000 pounds per square inch, and the elastic limit is only 5,000 pounds per square inch.

As for the uses of zinc, it can also be made into alloys in the construction industry and can be coated on the surface of iron sheets to make galvanized iron sheets, which are used to cover roofs. (End of Chapter 8)

Historical Talks on Architecture (IV) 198

— Buren

However, there was also a "Gothic Revival." People like Horace Walpole and Beckford were indeed very enthusiastic, but they were not very knowledgeable; they built strange houses for themselves. Although the spires and roof dust were mostly made of slats and plaster, and wooden window decorations were often simulated with paint to imitate stone, in their expectations, the appearance of these houses was in line with the correct medieval style. Of course, in these buildings, there are clumsy small windows, fragile and bizarre houses, and cold stone corridors, but such romantic houses gradually became popular. Even today, the British have not yet recovered from this epidemic; just look at the houses of the British today, which still cannot be separated from decorations such as small spires.

Thus, at the same time, even in the same place, you will find that one house belongs to the late classical style, another belongs to the fake Gothic style, and perhaps a third is a mixture of the two. This is the "Muddle Ages" of architecture. Now, we are still in this period, but at the same time we are working hard to get out of this period.

About fifty years ago, most people were surrounded by this "confusion," lazily imitating this or that, without intending to design buildings that were needed for actual life—this is proper architecture.

Later, Philip Webb and his successor Norman Shaw thought that it seemed like a very smart way to return to the benchmark that British architecture had reached before these different "revivals" broke the tradition. That is the architecture of the mid-eighteenth century, namely Georgian architecture. This architectural style gradually became popular, so the best British architecture in the past fifty years has belonged to this revived British classical style and its new variations. Now, there are many excellent architects, such as Sir Edwin Lutyens, who do not hesitate to solve new problems in their own way, although most of them base their new plans on the fashion of the eighteenth century. (To be continued)
